Current Commentary

Re-discussing British-Japanese Relations 26

— Ang

The other day, I discussed the conflict of interests between Britain and Japan in East Asia. In recent days, there have been two more events that can be used for reference. (1) Japan and Manchukuo signed an agreement on the 15th of this month in Changchun to establish a joint economic committee to "seek the permanent strengthening of economic relations between the two countries and the realization of the rational integration of the two countries' economies." This is another step in the East Asian Group Movement. (2) The Manchester Chamber of Commerce's textile, chemical, and machinery industries submitted a report on trade with China to the British Department of Commerce on the 17th of this month, confirming Japan's aggressive policies and commercial competition, making it necessary for Britain's laissez-faire policy in the Far East in recent years to be replaced by active action. This is another indication of the threat felt by the British side. The above two events are sharply opposed to each other. The seriousness of the economic conflict between the two countries can also be seen here.

Britain and Japan have such profound contradictions, but diplomacy is still hypocritical. Hirota's diplomacy has repeatedly used the word "cooperation" as its banner. The new British Foreign Secretary Hoare recently stated that in addition to maintaining Britain's Far Eastern interests, he is also willing to cooperate with Japan. This diplomatic state between the two countries is also worthy of consideration. First, let us talk about the essence of Hoare's political thought. When Baldwin reorganized the British cabinet, Hoare, as the Minister of Indian Affairs, succeeded Simon as Foreign Secretary. Eden was appointed as a minister without portfolio, specializing in League of Nations affairs. Hoare is a new figure in British diplomacy. His rise can be seen as a symbol of the British government's change of diplomatic policy, especially in its relations with the United States and Asia. According to our observation, Hoare's words and deeds since taking office as Foreign Secretary best represent the new British conservatism. In short, this doctrine is to seek the active development of its own interests in international compromise.

Last month, when the Japanese Ambassador to the United Kingdom, Matsudaira, left office and returned to his country, Hoare said a few words, roughly saying, "British-Japanese relations have recently had some factors of friction. Recent events in North China can be used to illustrate the rest. As the world's two major industrial countries, competition between industry and commerce is inevitable." He also said, "We in Britain believe that proper understanding and cooperation between the two countries is not only an element of Asian tranquility but also the key to world prosperity." From this perspective, Hoare seems to be still unable to forget British-Japanese cooperation, which is equally divided.

However, since the failure of the London Economic Conference, the attempt to seek world prosperity through international cooperation has become a dream that is hoped for but cannot be realized. Between Britain and Japan, since the abolition of the Indo-Japanese Commercial Treaty last year and the breakdown of the Simla Trade Conference, experts have long said that there is no room for reconciliation. Recently, the British government has repeatedly sought cooperation from the Japanese government in its move to send its chief economic advisor, Leith-Ross, to China, but Japanese Vice Foreign Minister Shigemitsu Kui has consistently refused, further proving that cooperation between the two countries is impossible. Then, are the so-called cooperation and collaboration in the diplomatic rhetoric of the two countries only to cover up the mutual hostility?

Italian-Ethiopian Dispute Enters a Serious Phase; British Ambassador Meets with Italian Prime Minister in Hopes of Salvage; Four-Point Plan Struggles to Satisfy Italian Desires; France Caught in a Dilemma, Unwilling to Abandon Old Friendship for New Acquaintance; Japan's Fickle Attitude Faces Attack from Italian Newspapers 27

(Rome) Sir Eric Drummond, the first Secretary-General of the League of Nations and current British Ambassador to Italy, plans to meet with Italian Prime Minister Mussolini today in a final effort to avert an Italian-Ethiopian war. However, Sir Drummond also stated that the Ethiopian Emperor's inflammatory speech has closed the door to a peaceful resolution. Nevertheless, diplomatic talks are continuing in a subdued atmosphere, while Mussolini continues to order the steamship "Arabia" to transport troops, supplies, and 580 mules to Africa, and has announced that, as of June 30th, Italy's military expenditure for the conquest of Africa has reached US$107,500,000. The plan proposed by Sir Drummond and the French Ambassador to Italy, Mr. Chambrun, to Mussolini includes the following four points: (1) Cession of Ethiopian border territory; (2) Italy to enjoy economic privileges in Ethiopia; (3) Italy to be allowed to build a railway through Ethiopian territory, connecting Eritrea and Italian Somaliland; (4) The Ethiopian government to employ Italian advisors, similar to Egypt's employment of British advisors. However, according to today's Italian newspaper editorials, one can clearly see Italy's attitude towards this kind of diplomatic negotiation. One newspaper stated that one thing has been determined in the dispute between Italy and Ethiopia, that is, the League of Nations has no right to interfere. (21st National Telegram)

(Also from Paris) French newspapers unanimously report that the Italian-Ethiopian dispute has entered a serious phase since the Ethiopian Emperor's recent passionate address to Parliament. A special dispatch from Rome in the "Petit Parisien" states that the severance of diplomatic relations between the two countries is not far off, but this does not necessarily mean that war will be declared or fighting will occur immediately. The "Paris Echo" believes that Japan's attitude of positioning itself as the protector of people of color is worthy of attention. Britain, having vast colonies in both Asia and Africa, is determined not to give them up easily. As this matter develops, Italy increasingly desires to strengthen its relations with France, as France is the only country that holds a pro-Italian attitude towards the Italian-Ethiopian conflict. However, Italy is not satisfied with France's neutrality and is now demanding further action from France. However, France itself is currently facing difficulties and, unless foolish, is unwilling to sacrifice its friendship with Britain for a new acquaintance like Italy. Mr. Bastié, Chairman of the Foreign Affairs Committee of the Chamber of Deputies, published an article in the "République" stating that Italy now wishes to rise above international organizations, an attitude that is tantamount to denying the existence or the right to self-determination of other countries, and will therefore endanger the entire concept of international order. (21st National Telegram)

British Cabinet Holds Meeting to Discuss the Italian-Ethiopian Issue 28

(London) Cabinet members held a meeting this morning, generally believed to be discussing the Abyssinian issue. (22nd Havas Telegram)

(London) According to the "Daily Telegraph," although some have argued that the Council of the League of Nations should seek to delay its meeting, London does not favor this. The crisis of an Italian-Ethiopian war is imminent, and to maintain peace, no further delay is appropriate. Therefore, the Council of the League of Nations should not postpone its meeting and waste this limited time. The report also stated, "What policy Britain will adopt is now being watched by all countries in the world. The United States government has requested to be notified at any time of Britain's attitude towards the Italian-Ethiopian dispute. As for the Soviet Union, it will not make any judgments on the Italian-Ethiopian dispute until Britain's policy is determined." The "Times" published a dispatch from its correspondent in Rome, which stated, "Last night, Italian newspapers published news that a conference of Britain, France, and Italy would be held in Rome in the shortest possible time. Italian officials have not heard of this. The news is technically correct because Britain, France, and Italy have not proposed holding what is normally called a 'conference.' However, according to the 1906 Three-Power Treaty on Abyssinia, any of the three countries (Britain, France, Italy) taking action regarding Abyssinia should consult with the other two countries beforehand. The Italian government can hardly refuse this kind of consultation. If Italian Prime Minister Mussolini holds consultations with the British and French Ambassadors to Italy in Rome, then, in all senses, although it is not a conference, it is no different from convening a three-nation conference. However, so far, the British and French governments have not instructed their ambassadors to Italy to hold consultations with the Italian Prime Minister. Therefore, the Abyssinian issue is currently in a stalemate, and the future is extremely chaotic. Everything is difficult to predict. The current rainy season in Abyssinia, which prevents military movement, is also one of the reasons for the chaotic situation." (22nd Havas Telegram)

Ethiopia Seeks Help from Britain; Negotiates for Loans to Cope with War and Requests Lifting of Arms Embargo 29

(London) The newly appointed Ethiopian Minister to Britain, Mr. Martin, recently gave an interview to a reporter from the "Daily Express," stating, "My purpose in coming to Britain is to obtain a loan. The Ethiopian government is in dire need of funds, not only to cope with the war but also to develop domestic mineral resources and other economic benefits. Ethiopia has extremely rich mineral reserves, and we are prepared to develop them." He also stated that if negotiations with British financial groups unfortunately fail, they plan to contact American capitalist Mr. Morgan, who is currently in Britain, to explore the possibility of obtaining loans from the United States. According to Martin, in addition to financial matters, his mission to Britain has two other purposes: one is to lobby the British government to support Ethiopia in the Italian-Ethiopian dispute and to work within the League of Nations to impose sanctions on Italy, such as blockading the Suez Canal to prevent Italian troops from passing through; the other is to request the British government to lift the embargo on arms to Ethiopia. Martin also detailed the Ethiopian military preparations in the interview, saying that they have stockpiled a large number of weapons and ammunition, such as machine guns, Lewis rifles, long-range field artillery, and anti-aircraft guns. As for poison gas, they will never use it because "such weapons may still be useful in Europe, but in our view, they are the mad actions of barbaric instincts." (22nd Havas Telegram)

Ethiopian Issue: Italy Demands Guarantees on Two Matters 30

(Paris) According to a statement by a former Italian Minister of Colonies, Italy's attitude towards the Italian-Ethiopian dispute can be summarized as follows: Italy does not value a resolution to this matter unless any resolution guarantees Italy two things: (1) "Security," not only guaranteeing the security of the Italian border but also gaining unlimited control over the Ethiopian military; (2) "Expansion," allowing Italy to colonize Ethiopia as France did with Morocco and Britain with Iraq, thereby civilizing Ethiopia. Italy is willing to resolve this matter peacefully, but it does not fear war and will not compromise on the resolution. Italy feels disappointed by the Treaty of Versailles and is now working to correct past mistakes. (22nd National Telegram)

Ethiopia's Strong Attitude; Ignores Italian Protest 31

Addis Ababa: The Ethiopian government has adopted an attitude of ignoring Mussolini's strong protest regarding the Ethiopian Emperor's inflammatory speech in Parliament. Therefore, the severance of diplomatic relations between the two countries is becoming increasingly imminent. (22nd National Telegram)

Detention of Prince Zema: Italy Uses it as a Pretext for Criticism; Ethiopian Government Responds to This 32

(London) Italian newspapers recently accused the Ethiopian Emperor of detaining the Prince of the Kingdom of Zema, intending to annex the country. Regarding this matter, the "Daily Telegraph" recently received a telegram from Addis Ababa, stating, "The Ethiopian government has responded to this accusation from Italy, mainly stating that it is true that the late King Abba Jiffar of Zema had designated his grandson Abba Shia as his successor. However, the Ethiopian Emperor revoked his right of succession because Abba Shia was incompetent, and he was also detained for participating in slave trafficking. Now, while foreigners oppose the slave system on the one hand, they defend the right to inherit the throne of slave traders on the other hand. The Ethiopian government is deeply surprised by this. The Kingdom of Zema was originally a stronghold of the slave system, and the Ethiopian government intends to reform it. Therefore, it directly exercises administrative power there to achieve effective reform. However, the so-called direct exercise of administrative power is completely different in nature from annexation. Outsiders cannot selectively quote it as a pretext for criticizing Ethiopia." (22nd Havas Telegram)

Japan's Fickle Actions: Italian Newspapers Unanimously Attack, Saying that Invoking the Kellogg-Briand Pact is Especially Disgusting 33

(Rome) Italian newspapers are now reacting strongly to Japan's attitude towards Ethiopia. The newspapers accuse Japan of trying to expand its commercial influence in East Africa, thereby harming Italy's interests. (22nd Reuters Telegram)

(Rome) Italian newspapers unanimously attack Japanese Foreign Minister Hirota's statement regarding the Italian-Ethiopian dispute, considering the Japanese government to be fickle and unprecedented. The "Messaggero" attacks Japan especially fiercely, stating, "Japanese Ambassador to Italy, Mr. Sugimura, just made a declaration, saying that Japan should remain neutral in the Italian-Ethiopian dispute, but before the ink was dry, he reversed himself, which is truly shocking. However, once the relationship between Japan and Italy is considered, it is not surprising at all. The Japanese government's sudden change of attitude is actually due to Japan's long-standing policy of hostility towards Italy. As for Japanese Ambassador Sugimura's visit to Mussolini, declaring neutrality in the Italian-Ethiopian dispute, it was actually due to accepting instructions from the Japanese government to deceive the Italian government (the motive for the deception is unknown). Unexpectedly, Sugimura took it seriously, and Foreign Minister Hirota had to deny it. In short, the reason why Japan is so concerned about the future of Ethiopia is due to two motives: one is due to commercial relations, and the other is due to racial relations. In terms of racial motives, its nature is very serious. All those who cherish the dignity of the white race must pay attention to it. We still remember that a spokesman for the Japanese government once declared that 'If Japan can sympathize with Ethiopia, it will be enough to increase Japan's commercial authority and political prestige among the black people in Africa and the Asian nations.' Moreover, for fifty years, Japanese politicians have repeatedly regarded the white race as Japan's enemy, so Japan's support for Ethiopia is indeed due to racial motives. As for Japan's proposal to invoke the Kellogg-Briand Pact to resolve the Italian-Ethiopian dispute, it is especially disgusting because Japan is now invading Chinese territory, and Chinese culture is more ancient and excellent than Japan's. Now that Japan is occupying China, shouldn't Italy be allowed to punish the barbaric Ethiopia?" "Il Piccolo" stated, "Japan's interference in the Italian-Ethiopian dispute is bizarre and misguided. However, in any case, Italy's position is very clear and firm. Japan's attitude, on the contrary, is enough to show the legitimacy of Mussolini's actions to Western countries and make people feel that action to protect European culture is, in fact, imperative." (22nd Havas Telegram)

British War Veterans Visit War Memorial; Old Battlefield Foes Meet and Greet, Refusing to Lay Wreath at Graves of Nazi Party Members 34

Munich: A grand ceremony was held today in front of the War Museum. A delegation of British war veterans visited the European War Memorial and paid tribute to the Munich soldiers who died in the European War. German war veterans' groups, carrying wartime banners, stood in formation around the memorial. The British delegation then inspected the various ranks of war veterans and shook hands with the seriously wounded to show respect. The British representatives also declared that today's respect for yesterday's enemies is not accidental; it is indeed admiration for the enemy's bravery. A miracle that could not be believed a few years ago will now become a thing of the past. Enemies who fought each other yesterday now stand shoulder to shoulder, without any animosity, paying tribute to the soldiers who died in the European War to commemorate them. After the ceremony, the British delegation went to the headquarters of the Nazi Party to listen to the history of the Nazi Party's past struggles. Afterwards, they attended a reception hosted by the Mayor of Munich, where they were warmly welcomed by the Mayor. After the banquet, the British delegation split into groups to tour. (21st National Social Telegram)

(Paris) The British war veterans' delegation went from Berlin to Munich yesterday to visit the "Brown House," the birthplace of the Nazi Party. Someone asked them to lay a wreath in front of the monument to the Nazi Party members who died in the November 29, 1923 coup. The British delegation refused to do so because they believed that this act had political implications. The "Paris Echo" recently published a telegram from its correspondent in London, stating that the British delegation, after this provocation, will inevitably return disappointed after going in with high spirits. The British war veterans' delegation went to Munich at the invitation of the German side, and the German side did not inform them of the purpose of the visit beforehand. When they arrived there, they were asked to lay a wreath in front of the monument to the Nazi Party members. The British delegation believed that this kind of expression had political implications and was inconvenient to participate in, so they politely declined. Although the Nazi Party authorities were rejected, they kept it secret until the scheduled time, when the crowd gathered in front of the monument. The German war veterans temporarily placed a wreath there as a cover. Therefore, the general public still thought that it was a wreath laid by the British. Even the German newspapers misrepresented the facts and believed it to be true. (21st Havas Telegram)

Conflict Between German Party and Church Becomes Increasingly Acute; Catholic Churches Throughout Germany Read Declaration Resisting Hitler's Religious Policies 35

(Berlin) The conflict between the German Nazi Party and the Catholic Church is now becoming increasingly acute. Catholic priests have openly resisted General Goering's order to crack down on political Catholicism. Yesterday, hundreds of priests, disregarding the danger of being imprisoned, read essays from the Vatican newspaper on the church platform, condemning the Nazi Party's destruction of the treaty between Germany and the Vatican. This essay defended the Catholic youth movement and the Catholic labor organization, and criticized the destruction of reproductive function and Interior Minister Frick's statement that German Catholics must abide by national laws, even laws that are against religion and morality. Yesterday, secret detectives were deployed in Berlin churches, but the Nazi Party authorities have not yet decided on a way to arrest the priests on a large scale. The Nazi Party apparently attacks both German Jews and Catholics in unison, without distinction. General Goering's order to crack down on political Catholicism has been promulgated nationwide. The Minister of Education has reissued an instruction stating that this order must be implemented, regardless of who they are or the position of the church. At the same time, the court has been instructed to severely punish dangerous elements that could harm the country and the people. The "Münchner Neueste Nachrichten" reported from Berlin that the Nazi Party's anti-religious plan and the plan to disband the Stahlhelm are progressing simultaneously. The Nazi Party considers the Stahlhelm to be a conservative restorationist organization with no anti-Semitic nature. Furthermore, the public is gradually feeling the impact of Germany's economic difficulties and the loss of foreign trade. The Nazi Party's actions against Jews and religion and its crackdown on the Stahlhelm are probably also intended to divert public attention. (22nd Reuters Telegram)

Brussels: According to news obtained by the "Nation Belge" on the Belgian-German border, a wave of anti-Nazi sentiment has recently occurred in Aachen, a city in western Germany, and the situation is very tense. Aachen has always been a Catholic stronghold, and the Catholics have always lacked goodwill towards the Nazi Party. Recently, several nuns were arrested for smuggling money. At the same time, a certain professor was also arrested on suspicion of being an accomplice. This has aroused resentment from the Catholic Church, and the entire city is extremely uneasy. The Nazi Party authorities are deeply afraid of accidents and have strictly defended the barracks of the Party Army. (21st Havas Telegram)

Anti-Semitic Movement Continues Unabated 36

(Berlin) Members of the Nazi Party's assault troops clashed with Jews on Kurfürstendamm here several times last week, but today the situation there is no longer turbulent, and the situation is slightly more stable. Jewish customers are no longer seen in front of cafes, and the "assault troop groups" against Jews no longer march in teams to demonstrate. There are also no more slogans on the street saying "Jews insult the German race." However, anti-Semitic disturbances continue to occur in the area around Bavariaplatz. Nazi Party members wrote in large letters in front of the shops opened by Jews there, "I am a Jew. German people who come here to buy will be in danger." In addition, a Swedish film called "Pettersson und Bendel," whose content is based on the anti-Semitic movement, is considered by the Propaganda Department to have "political value" and has been authorized to be shown in various places tax-free. The film has recently been reprinted in multiple copies and sent to various places for screening. It is also reported here that the anti-Semitic movement is very active in the provinces. For example, in Trieste, Jewish shops are limited to closing at 5:00 PM every day. Crowds march in teams, shouting "Jews, die quickly" or "German women, don't have relations with pigs (referring to Jews)." The names of all women who have been with Jews are disclosed in the newspapers. Some public places also have signs hanging at the entrance saying "Dogs and Jews are not allowed in." (21st Havas Telegram)

(New York) A Jewish banker here named Felix Warburg has initiated the organization of a "Refugee Economic Corporation" whose purpose is to take in Jews who have been abused in Germany or other countries, so that they can take refuge in the United States. The company's capital is set at US$10 million and will be raised publicly. (21st Havas Telegram)

Greek Royalists Deny Restoration Coup; Confident of Victory in Plebiscite; Mayor of Athens Visits Exiled King in London 37

Athens: The Restoration Party here firmly denies rumors of a restoration coup. The Restoration Party is confident that a majority of people will support restoration in the upcoming plebiscite. (21st Reuters Telegram)

Athens: In view of the instability of the domestic political situation, the Greek government has banned all public demonstrations. However, officials are trying their best to deny the rumors that a coup is about to occur to restore the monarchy, saying that the royal family has no reason to take risks now, as the victory in the autumn vote will ultimately belong to the monarchists. Newspapers here deny the rumors in foreign newspapers about the exiled King George's conspiracy to stage a coup, saying that the former king is mature and prudent and will be able to wait patiently for the government to complete its plebiscite. (22nd National Telegram)

(London) The Mayor of Athens, Mr. Kotsias, came to England a few days ago to visit the exiled King George II of Greece to discuss the domestic political situation and report on public opinion regarding the issue of restoration. Today, Mr. Kotsias and the exiled King held talks, which lasted for six hours. (21st Havas Telegram)

Indian Muslim Riot; Situation Remains Serious; British Troops Deployed as if Facing a Major Enemy, Firing Live Ammunition and Causing Bloodshed 38

(London) According to news reported by the "Daily Telegraph," a riot suddenly occurred in Lahore, India, yesterday. At that time, ten people were killed and 74 people were injured, including five British police officers. The situation of this rebellion is the most serious in years. Although the military and police tried their best to suppress it after the incident last night, the rebellion is still rampant, and the entire city has suddenly become uneasy. Furthermore, the Muslim people of Amritsar in Punjab are on strike to express their sympathy for the rebellion. A large number of soldiers and police were deployed to suppress it, so there was no tragedy of bloodshed. (22nd Havas Telegram)

Lahore: Yesterday, Muslims attacked the military and police, causing great disturbance. The situation is still serious today, so more British troops were deployed in the afternoon to suppress them. The troops placed barbed wire nets in the streets to prevent the Muslims from attacking. However, the Muslims still did not disperse at night. This morning, the number of people suddenly increased by several thousand, and the momentum was fierce. They threw bricks and stones at the soldiers. The authorities' warning was ineffective. At noon, the soldiers fired six shots, but the Muslims still resisted the soldiers and threw stones at them again. The British soldiers then fired live ammunition again, killing about two people. The demonstrators' arrogance was slightly reduced, but their attitude is still strong. The Lahore Light Cavalry of Punjab was also deployed to assist, and the Sixth Lancers and the Sixth Armored Car Regiment were ordered to station in the park to prevent accidents. British troops are now stationed in all important places in Lahore, and armored vehicles travel back and forth on the main thoroughfares. It is reported that a total of 16 people have died in the riots, and the number of injured is quite large. (21st Reuters Telegram)

The Rise of Trade Wars: Britain and America Reject Japanese Goods; Britain Encourages Imperial Markets to Prevent Dumping; America Considers Import Restrictions on Japanese Cotton Cloth 39

(Tokyo) The Egyptian government's abrogation of the trade treaty with Japan is actually orchestrated by Britain. This oppressive policy adopted by Britain was decided after the breakdown of the Anglo-Japanese private cotton industry cooperative. Moreover, its instigation is not limited to Egypt. "Palestine," nearby "Transjordan," and "Iraq," which is under British control, are all being influenced by British merchants through the power of the aforementioned governments. Britain is also encouraging British Imperial markets and those in Central and South America to prevent the import of Japanese goods. In the current state of affairs, it is impossible for Japanese cotton products to develop new markets. Even maintaining the current situation will become impossible. To protect the existing market for cotton products and to attempt reasonable development, the idea of reopening the Anglo-Japanese private sector conference has recently resurfaced. (Twenty-second Dispatch from the Electric Communication Society)

Ottawa: After the report that the Japanese government is launching a trade protection law reached here, Canada's government and public are quite shocked. In particular, the western regions such as British Columbia, which are directly affected, are advocating retaliatory measures against Japan. (Twentieth Dispatch from the Japanese Allied Press)

(Tokyo) It is reported that Canada is considering levying an additional tax of one-third ad valorem or abrogating the trade treaty based on the provisions of the tariff law in response to Japan's launch of the Trade Protection Act. The Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs is also studying countermeasures with a cautious attitude. However, if Canada adopts a challenging attitude, Japan is determined to fight a tariff war. If Canada raises tariffs, Japan will increase the current 50% additional tax to 100% or add other goods in accordance with the provisions of the Trade Protection Act to counterattack. If Canada abrogates the trade treaty and treats Japanese goods in a discriminatory manner, Japan will also impose discriminatory tariffs on Canadian goods and adopt a policy of prohibiting Canadian goods from entering the country. However, in terms of Japan-Canada trade tariffs, Japan's exports to Canada in the past year were only 8.66 million yuan, while Canada's exports to Japan reached 54 million yuan. Therefore, the impact on the Canadian side is greater than that on the Japanese side. It is expected that the Canadian side will not abrogate the trade treaty and will continue diplomatic negotiations. The Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs knows that Canada's strong demands will be difficult to sustain. Therefore, it is determined to persist in a tough confrontation to prompt Canada to reflect. (Twenty-second Dispatch from the Electric Communication Society)

(Tokyo) It is reported that the United States will adopt import restrictions on Japanese cotton products. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs has the following views on this intention: It is true that American textile manufacturers are advocating raising tariffs or implementing restrictions to prevent the import of Japanese cotton cloth. Regarding this matter, Ambassador Saito has repeatedly visited Secretary Hull to request understanding. Although the United States pointed out that Japanese cotton cloth is flooding the entire American market and that imports of Japanese cotton cloth account for 17% of the total, the United States should also consider the large amount of American cotton imported into Japan and the great benefit to the American agricultural community. This time, the movement is a compromise proposal because Japan has withdrawn the increase in the processing tax on rayon products from the Lyon region. It is also unknown whether it will take the form of import restrictions or become a matter for Congress. However, as no official telegram has been received, it is impossible to express an attitude. (Twenty-second Dispatch from the Electric Communication Society)

The Japanese Covet the Kailuan Coal Mines; Japanese Newspapers Report British Interest in Transferring Ownership 42

(Tokyo) The Kailuan Coal Mines, the center of British power in North China, have been affected by pressure from the Fushun Coal Mine and the Xishan Coal Mine, as well as the economic downturn. Last year, the coal mine and its associated businesses suffered losses of approximately 400,000 yuan. Furthermore, Britain is considering the expansion of Japanese power along the Beining Line and that it will be more difficult to revive the business in the future. Therefore, Japanese newspapers reported that Britain intends to transfer the rights and interests of the Kailuan Coal Mines and its affiliated businesses to Japan, making it a joint venture between China, Britain, and Japan. Changben, wanting to develop the North China economy, intends to take control of the port of Qinhuangdao, so it is also very eager to operate the mines.

Note: The Kailuan Coal Mines are located in the area of ​​Tangshan Guye Station along the Beining Railway, eleven kilometers north and south, including the coal mines of Tangshan, Xishan, Linxi, Majiagou, Zhaogezhuang, Yinzikou, Langweigou, Chenjialing, and Taoyuan. The average coal seam is thirteen to thirty-four meters thick, and the deepest reaches seventy-six meters. The reserves are approximately 325 million tons. The coal quality is bituminous coal. In the years before and after the September 18th Incident, the annual production was 3 million to 4.5 million tons. If estimated based on the previous production standards, it can still be mined for a hundred years. (Twenty-second Dispatch from the China United News Agency)

Sino-French-Vietnamese Treaty: Both Sides Announce Implementation 51

(Nanjing) A large number of our compatriots reside in Vietnam. In the past, they suffered greatly because no consulates were established. Now the Sino-French-Vietnamese Treaty has been announced and implemented by both sides. Article 3 of the treaty stipulates that the Chinese government may station consuls in Hanoi or Haiphong and Saigon in Vietnam. It is reported that our government intends to establish consulates in Vietnam to protect the interests of overseas Chinese. The location of the future consulates will be in Saigon and Hanoi, but it is still under consideration. (Twenty-second Dispatch from the Central News Agency)

(Nanjing) The Special Treaty on Relations between Vietnam and the Border Provinces of China and its appendices, which have been recently agreed upon by China and France, were announced and implemented by both parties on the 22nd and have been reported in various newspapers. According to a diplomatic expert familiar with the process of this negotiation, the main treaty of the Special Treaty on Relations between Vietnam and the Border Provinces of China was signed by former Foreign Minister Wang Zhengting and former French Ambassador Martell on May 16, 1930. Subsequently, work began on discussing Tables A and B contained in the first annex to the treaty. Table A contains more than 30 kinds of important goods from the southwestern border provinces of China, which, when transported from Yunnan, Guangxi, and Guangdong to Vietnam, can be taxed at the lowest tariff rate. Table B contains goods from French Vietnam that, when transported to the above three provinces, can be taxed in accordance with China's tariffs at the time. Initially, the French proposal reportedly also included dozens of items. After several disputes, the French side finally agreed to reduce it to six taxable items and agreed to use the tariffs at the time of the formal signing of the goods table as the standard. However, it insisted that the item of white coal produced in Vietnam in Table B should be taxed according to the previous tax rate and stated that if this issue could not be resolved, the negotiations would be impossible to proceed. The government did not agree to the request because the coal tax had already been increased at that time. After repeated consultations, the negotiations were on the verge of breaking down. In 1933, the government considered that the completion of the Vietnamese treaty was related to the entire Sino-Vietnamese commerce and the interests of overseas Chinese in Vietnam. It had no choice but to make slight concessions. It reached an agreement with the French side that within the validity period of this special treaty, the import of Vietnamese white coal could be taxed according to the 1932 tax rate, and an exchange of documents was immediately made to clearly define Vietnamese white coal, so that only the components of Vietnamese anthracite white coal would match it, in order to show restrictions. The issue of the Vietnamese coal import tax was thus resolved. At that time, China was collecting rice tax and increasing the tax rate. The French side then requested the unification of the rice tax and the reduction of the tax amount because of the large amount of Vietnamese rice imported. The signing of the two appendices, A and B, went through another twist. Afterwards, after repeated consultations, the government, always for the sake of the entire Sino-Vietnamese commercial relationship and the maintenance of the interests of overseas Chinese in Vietnam, again agreed to the French side's determination of a tax amount that was not much different from the current tax rate, and only for a period of two years. The rice tax issue was also brought to a close. Thus, all the points of contention on both sides were resolved. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the French Ambassador Weili signed the protocol on the conclusion of the two appendices A and B and other annexes on May 4 of this year. The written records of the entire treaty and its annexes were signed and exchanged instruments of ratification by our Acting Charge d'Affaires in France Xiao Jirong and representatives of the French Ministry of Foreign Affairs in Paris on July 20. The treaty was announced and implemented on the 22nd. The Vietnamese treaty, which had been desired by the government and the public for many years, was thus completed. According to the provisions of the treaty and its annexes, the most important benefits obtained by China are the following: (1) The more than 30 kinds of Chinese goods listed in the above-mentioned Table A, when transported from China to Vietnam, can be taxed at the lowest tax rate; (2) A large number of overseas Chinese reside in Vietnam, and they have suffered greatly because no consulates have been established. After the implementation of the new treaty, China can station consuls in Saigon and Hanoi or Haiphong to protect overseas Chinese; (3) The Vietnamese government has often discriminated against overseas Chinese and treated them harshly, especially in matters such as entry and relocation. After the implementation of the new treaty, overseas Chinese will enjoy most-favored-nation treatment when entering and leaving Vietnam and traveling in the interior. They will also be treated the same as most-favored-nation nationals in terms of paying various taxes; (4) Various privileges historically enjoyed by overseas Chinese, such as land rights, navigation rights, and fishing rights, can be more clearly guaranteed after the implementation of the new treaty, so that they will not be deprived at any time; (5) The transit tax levied on Chinese goods passing through Vietnam has in fact been levied up to 20%. After the implementation of the new treaty, the transit tax can be reduced or exempted separately, and the increase in Chinese goods exported to Vietnam and the prosperity of commerce in Yunnan, Guangxi, and Guangdong are all the more a matter of course. (Twenty-second Dispatch from the Central News Agency)

(Paris) Xiao Jirong, Counselor of our Embassy in France, went to the French Ministry of Foreign Affairs on the morning of the 20th at 11:00 to sign the Vietnamese treaty and exchange records (Process Verbal) and received the original treaty. The French side was approved by Prime Minister and Minister of Foreign Affairs Laval. Both sides will announce it on the 22nd of this month, and it will take effect immediately. (Twenty-first Dispatch from the Central News Agency)

The Yangzi Company's Closure Dispute: Compromise Mediation Solution 52

(Nanjing) After the closure of the Yangzi Flour Company, the results of consultations between various agencies on the 22nd were that since the company was closed due to financial losses and inability to support itself, there are in fact no funds available to resume operations. Representatives of various agencies held a small group meeting before the talks to determine a reasonable compromise solution. According to the labor side's demands, all workers must be paid one and a half years' wages. The factory side only agreed to give one month's wages in accordance with the provisions of the Factory Law. The representatives, considering the difficulties of both labor and management, determined a comprehensive solution. The main points are: 1. All workers will be paid two and a half months' wages; 2. The factory will issue certificates of employment, and they will have priority in employment when operations resume; 3. The 6,000 bags of flour stored in the factory when the Datong Flour Mill leased the factory will be allowed to be released and taken back by Datong itself. Representatives of the party and government agencies will go to the factory this afternoon to announce this plan and set a deadline of 10:00 a.m. on the 23rd to receive replies from both parties in order to sign the agreement and implement it. It is reported that the company's debts are about 1 million yuan, with the China Industrial Bank being the largest creditor. Several companies such as Zhejiang Xingye Salt Industry National Goods Shanghai and others are temporary commodity mortgage loans with small amounts. As for the machinery and other equipment, they were mortgaged to the China Industrial Bank long ago. As far as the hope of resuming operations is concerned, Yangzi itself has no way to do so. (Twenty-second Special Dispatch)

Customs Administration Expenses to be Paid in Three Parts 54

(Nanjing) Wu Jing, Chief of the Customs Administration Section of the Ministry of Finance, reported that the expenditure of the Customs Administration is divided into three parts: (1) the Customs Service, (2) the Customs Superintendent, and (3) the Customs School. (1) The original budget for the Customs Service for the 24th year was 34 million yuan (including anti-smuggling expenses). The Central Political Committee reviewed it and first reduced it to 32 million yuan, and then reduced it to 30 million yuan, a sudden reduction of 4 million yuan, which is quite insufficient. It is now striving to tighten expenses to adapt to the situation. According to the customs expenses of various countries, the ratio of customs expenses to tax revenue is between 1% and 10%. China's current customs revenue is about 30 million yuan per year. Increasing the anti-smuggling effectiveness will minimize tax evasion, while reducing the anti-smuggling effectiveness will expand the scope of tax evasion. It is also unknown whether the result of reducing expenditure will be penny-wise and pound-foolish. (2) There are a total of 28 Customs Superintendent offices nationwide. The budget for the 24th year is 670,000 yuan, which the Central Political Committee reviewed and reduced to 570,000 yuan, which is very tight. It was originally prepared to abolish the inland transit customs, but now, because the abolition of transit and exemption of export taxes cannot be implemented for a while, it has been decided to start with a general reduction in expenditure. The current monthly expenses of each customs post are 3,000 yuan for those with more expenses and 1,000 yuan for those with fewer expenses. (3) The Customs School, including the Beiping Main School and the Shanghai Branch School, has achieved excellent results in the past. Most of those who now serve in the Customs Service are graduates of the school. Due to the overcrowding of customs personnel, graduates cannot be placed, coupled with financial constraints, it has been decided to suspend the Beiping Main School from this semester and merge it into the Shanghai Branch School, saving 50,000 yuan per year, which has been approved by the Minister. (Twenty-second Special Dispatch)

International Commercial Telegram, July 22nd, Reuter's Special Commercial News

Gold and Silver: The London gold price today is 140 shillings and 8.5 pence, down 4 pence.

London Silver Market: Stable today. The spot price is 30 pence and 1875, and the futures price is 30 pence and 3125, both unchanged. Speculators sold, while the United States and India bought.

Mangalore Silver: Futures opened today. September saw differences, with some lower by 15 pounds from Saturday's close and others higher by 25 pounds. Market conditions were light.

Exchange Rates: US-UK: In the London foreign exchange market this morning, the US dollar price showed a strengthening trend. The US-UK exchange rate was 4 dollars, 96 and 375/1000 cents, lower by 125/10000 from Saturday's US-UK close. It continued to fall by 0625/10000 after the first hour, reaching 4 dollars, 96 and 3125/10000 cents. This price remained unchanged until 2:00 PM. Liu Hangchen, Director of the Sichuan Finance Department, Discusses Sichuan Finance and Disarmament 79

Tightening Expenses to Balance Revenue and Expenditure is Hoped For, 120,000 Troops Have Been Disbanded

Nanjing Correspondence: Liu Hangchen, Director of the Sichuan Finance Department, and Guan Jiyu, Special Finance Commissioner, flew to Nanjing yesterday to request detailed methods for reorganizing Sichuan finance from the Ministry of Finance. This reporter visited Mr. Liu and had a long conversation of one hour, discussing the financial situation and troop reduction in Sichuan in detail. The following is a record (what follows is Mr. Liu's talk):

Regarding Sichuan's financial situation, first, on the expenditure side, it can be roughly divided into four items: The regular expenses of the original troops were about 60 million yuan per year, the bandit suppression expenses were about 18 million yuan, the debt repayment fund was 12.2 million yuan, and the administrative expenses were 11 million yuan, totaling over 100 million yuan. Now, after reorganizing the remaining troops, tightening expenditures, and with the Military Affairs Commission bearing the bandit suppression expenses, the expenditure figures are: regular troop expenses of about 40 million yuan per year, a debt repayment fund of 12.2 million yuan, and administrative expenses of 11 million yuan, totaling about 63.3 million yuan. Second, on the revenue side, the original revenue figures were: salt tax (including surcharges) of about 15 million yuan per year, land tax of over 7.5 million yuan, special military levies of over 22.7 million yuan, special taxes of 12 million yuan, local taxes of 15 million yuan, stamp, tobacco, and alcohol taxes of over 3 million yuan, miscellaneous taxes of 4.3 million yuan, and slaughter tax of 1.8 million yuan, totaling about 81 million yuan. Due to the bandit disturbances in the north and south, revenue has sharply decreased. The current revenue figures are: salt tax (including surcharges) of about 10.3 million yuan per year, land tax of over 6.9 million yuan, special military levies of over 20.7 million yuan, special taxes of over 9 million yuan, local taxes of over 12 million yuan, stamp, tobacco, and alcohol taxes of over 3 million yuan, miscellaneous taxes of 4.3 million yuan, and slaughter tax of 1.8 million yuan, totaling about 68 million yuan. However, as the authorities are striving to reduce expenditures, and with all expenses being tightened, it can still be managed. This is the general situation of Sichuan's financial revenue and expenditure.

Striving to Save Expenditures: When I (Mr. Liu referring to himself) returned to Sichuan, the monthly military expenses of the troops directly under the command of Liu FuCheng, the Sichuan Rehabilitation Supervisor, had reached over 2.94 million yuan. At that time, Supervisor Liu immediately and voluntarily reduced the number of officers and soldiers by about 30,000, reducing the military expenses to over 2.4 million yuan. After February, it was voluntarily reduced again to over 2.1 million yuan. After the various armies handed over their defense zones in March, including the military expenses of each army, it totaled over 3.7 million yuan. Adding clothing and other miscellaneous expenses, the total regular expenses of the various units were about 4.2 million yuan per month. The total amount of military agencies and military supplementary expenses was 783,000 yuan per month. Combined, the annual regular expenses were about 60 million yuan.

Sichuan Army Limited to Reorganization: Today, Sichuan's finances have the hope of balancing revenue and expenditure, the key to which lies entirely in troop reduction. Therefore, on June 30th, Chairman Chiang issued the "30 Secret Chengdu Telegram" ordering a reduction of one-third, to be completed before July 15th. Before I came east this time, according to news from all sides, the expenses reduced by the reorganization have reached 15 million yuan per year. Supervisor Liu also flew to Chongqing on the 18th of this month to make every effort to tighten military agencies and military supplementary expenses. The limit set by the Chairman's telegram can be easily achieved in the shortest possible time.

Finances After Reorganization: After this reorganization, Sichuan's finances will have a surplus, which will be used in the first step to repay the debts incurred by the provincial government when it took over the defense zones in the shortest possible time, as well as future revenue from sources such as house rent and business tax. The second step will be to transfer the remaining funds to construction expenses. The expenses for this reorganization will only amount to 1.4 million yuan, as stipulated by Chairman Chiang. Even if there is an increase in the future, the amount will be limited. This is all due to the thorough understanding of the military commanders, so they were able to reorganize over 120,000 troops in the shortest period of 15 days and with the least expense of 1.4 million yuan. It is only with the determination of Chairman Chiang that this achievement could be reached, even with the most intense bandit suppression going on in the front lines.

Coming to Nanjing to Request Instructions on Reorganization Methods: The Chairman has already ordered the implementation of the reorganization. In terms of reducing expenditures, we have succeeded. This time, I was ordered to come east to request detailed methods for reorganizing finances from the Ministry of Finance in order to follow them. I have decided to go to Shanghai tonight and will return to Sichuan in a week. How the final measures will be determined, I will inform you again later. Today, rural bankruptcy and reducing the burden on the people are the unanimous demands of the entire country. In handling Sichuan's finances, I should also do my best in this regard. Everything under the provincial government has already been reduced, and everything under the provincial government is currently being investigated and reported by the counties according to the methods promulgated by the Military Affairs Commission. Over 90 counties have already submitted reports, accounting for about two-thirds of the province. When I return to Sichuan, I will do my best to start reorganizing county and city local finances. As for the bandit suppression situation, it has been recorded in various newspapers. Recently, important locations such as Tumen and Diexi have been successively recovered, and the bandit areas have been completely locked down. The future is promising, and so on.

Smuggling Foreign Rice Flows into Chaoshan 80

The Right to Transport and Sell Grain in Shantou City Will Be Controlled by a Certain Foreigner

Shantou Correspondence: The monthly import of foreign rice into Shantou is no less than 100,000 bags. Currently, rice merchants, in response to the boycott of Siamese rice, have mostly switched to importing and selling Annam and Rangoon rice. In the first half of July, only 2,150 bags of Siamese rice were imported. However, a certain foreigner in Shantou is taking this opportunity to jointly establish a rice shop, planning to directly charter ships to transport rice from Siam to Shantou for distribution. Relying on special preferential trade agreements, the foreigner does not pay the special agricultural product tax when the rice arrives in Shantou. The North-South lines, charter lines, and grain lines of Shantou are greatly panicked upon hearing this news and have held several meetings and telegraphed the provincial government to inquire about countermeasures. This is because the foreign rice imported by our own people is subject to a special tax of more than three yuan per bag, while the rice imported by the foreigner is not subject to special taxes. Moreover, they have opened retail shops in Qi Lu, which are very prosperous. If the market price is twelve catties of rice per yuan, they sell seventeen or eighteen catties. Most of those who buy are poor people, some coming from as far as Chenghai Oumen and Chaoan Anbu to buy in Shantou. The foreigner has a protective amulet, and the tax bureau inspectors dare not interfere. Most of the rice buyers are poor people, so there is no way to restrict them from buying good rice. Yesterday, the Japanese ship "Guangdong Maru" and the Chaozhou ship arrived in Shantou from Hong Kong, carrying the 15th batch of Siamese rice, more than 800 bags. After being unloaded at the customs and inspected by customs officials, it was transported by freight car to the foreigner's rice shop on Xinxing Road in Qi Lu. The inspectors looked aside, and passersby were amazed. As smuggled rice is continuously being imported, the market price of rice has plummeted. According to rice merchants, the foreigner can make a profit of 20% on each yuan's worth of tax-free rice, while domestic merchants will lose money on the rice they import at thirteen catties per yuan. However, given the situation, even at a loss, they must sell the rice, otherwise they will have to pay warehouse rent, and the rice will be damaged by rats and insects over time. It is better to sell it all at a loss at once, temporarily suspend business, and wait for the government to resolve the issue. If the government has no solution, the Chinese grain shops will have to wait for their demise. The right to transport and sell grain will henceforth be transferred to the foreigner's hands, which is truly heartbreaking. (July 17th)

Songjiang: Water Police Patrol and Seize Smuggled Opium

He Tu, the leader of the second squad of the third team of the first district of the Water Police Provincial Public Team, led patrol officers Gu Lansheng and others on patrol through Sijing, Qibao, and reached the Fengjing Xinbang area. On the 21st, based on a report that Zhai Xingrang in the area was suspected of selling opium and operating a private opium den, they quietly led officers and police to search the premises and seized more than ten taels of smuggled opium, 8.7 qian of official opium, opium pipes, and many other items. With both the person and the evidence in hand, they took them back to the squad headquarters for interrogation and then prepared a document to transfer them to the county government on the 22nd for legal action.

Suzhou: Demolition of Enclosed Fields Causes Riot Among Tenant Farmers

The enclosure of lake fields in East Taihu, carried out jointly by the governments of Wu County and Wujiang County, dispatched provincial security teams and over 7,000 villagers to demolish the enclosures. All the enclosed fields and embankments of various companies, such as Gongcheng, Minsheng, and Nankai, have been completely demolished. However, on the 21st, during the demolition, near Nankai, over 200 tenant farmers who had enclosed 70 shares suddenly beat gongs and fired guns, intending to riot and obstruct the demolition. Fortunately, battalion adjutant Nie led the team to deploy carefully, and the tenant farmers could not succeed. The security team arrested 14 rioting tenant farmers, including Fang Zongxian, and Wujiang also arrested two, all of whom were detained at the team headquarters. The county government has submitted a request to the province for instructions on how to handle the matter. The magistrates of Wujiang and Wu County will discuss how to handle the remaining issues immediately.

Wuxi: Flour Boat Encounters Bandits in Taihu Lake

Zhou Xingquan, from Jiangxiqiao in the southern suburbs of this county, has been transporting flour for the Maoxin Flour Company. On the 21st, his barge was fully loaded with flour and transported to Huzhou, Zhejiang. After unloading the goods, he was sailing back to Wuxi when he encountered a bandit boat near the Shushankou Wutangmen area of Taihu Lake. Seven bandits jumped out, one with a pistol and the others with sharp blades, ordering the boat to stop. They arbitrarily searched and robbed. When crew members Xu Ape and Apan slightly resisted, they were stabbed three times, injuring their hands, but not seriously. On the 22nd, they sailed to the city and reported to the Public Security Bureau to request the arrest of the bandits and the recovery of the stolen goods.

Changzhou: Jiang Tide Rises Sharply, Embankments in Danger

Dehe Township in the third district of Wuyi County is mostly sandy fields. The residents there rely on dikes for protection. Recently, due to the sharp increase in the Yangtze River water level and the period of strong tides, the residents of each dike feel uneasy. A section of Xitaishun Dike in the third Bao of the township was breached by the river tide, about two Zhang long. The water rushed in, and the soybean seedlings in the dike were all submerged. Fortunately, the nearby police station supervised the Baojia heads and able-bodied men to work hard to block the breach, and it took three hours to close the breach. However, the adjacent Nanxing Dike, Dadunzi Dike, and Dongheshun Dike were all under heavy pressure from the river tide, and their current condition is dangerous. Several breaches have already occurred. If the river tide continues to surge, the collapse of the dikes is a concern. They are conscientiously preventing and blocking the breaches daily, and the Xiaochehe Public Security branch office reported to the county bureau on the 21st for instructions.

Yangzhou: Investigation of Baojia Reveals Bizarre Case

Dong Xueti, the chief of the third Bao of Huangjin Township in the ninth district of Jiangdu, discovered two suspicious men and women while compiling and investigating the Baojia at the home of Zhou Chengye in Yanting Village. He took them to the town office, where Shi, who was representing the town chief, inquired and learned that the man was named Wu Xuerong and the woman was named Cuiying. They had worked in Shanghai and returned home together and were temporarily staying with Zhou because they were relatives. Just as they were about to be sent to the district office, a person from Qianjiashan came to the town claiming that a daughter had been lost many years ago and suspected that she was Cuiying. He brought a photo of a girl slightly resembling Cuiying for comparison. There was only a one- or two-point resemblance in the eyebrows, so he confirmed that Cuiying was his daughter. Cuiying also recognized him as her father, so Qiu Yongkang, the Jia head of Baocheng Township, vouched for her. Later, Qian saw that Cuiying's behavior was not like that of his daughter. Then, blacksmith Qiu Ruhai recognized Cuiying as his wife and went directly to the Public Security Detective Team to report. The detective captain Hu Keyin has now taken all the witnesses to the team for interrogation. It is not yet known what the truth is.

Zhenjiang: Provincial Chamber of Commerce Holds Executive and Supervisory Meeting

The Jiangsu Provincial Chamber of Commerce also held a joint executive and supervisory meeting in Zhenjiang on the afternoon of the 21st, chaired by Yu Shichuan. Matters discussed included: (1) A letter from the Third Section of the Construction Department stating that this province is scheduled to convene a representative meeting of various trade associations for silk, cloth, and spun yarn on August 1st and 2nd, regarding matters that should be established and reformed in each industry, hoping that proposals will be submitted by each industry for discussion. How should this be handled? It was resolved that Mr. Qian Sunqing should draft the silk industry plan, Mr. Cheng Ganqing should draft the silk fabric industry plan, and Mr. Lin Junbao and Mr. Wu Shuying should draft the cotton yarn fabric industry plan. All should be submitted to the association for transfer to the department within five days. (2) A letter from the Beijing Municipal Chamber of Commerce and the Wu County Chamber of Commerce requesting a joint petition for the promulgation and implementation of the Stamp Tax Law. How should this be handled? It was resolved to pass the proposal. (3) It was resolved to convene the fourth members' meeting on October 1st, with the meeting period set for two days.

Haimen: Steam Boiler Explosion Injures Five People

Chen Hesheng Dyehouse in Hehe Town, District 5, has been open for many years and has been quite successful. Recently, in order to improve its products and compete with its peers, it purchased new-style machinery and hired five technicians. On the morning of the 20th, the machinery was completely installed, and they began dyeing cloth. However, the quality of the steam boiler was poor, and it suddenly exploded. Iron pieces flew in all directions, and five technicians, including Zhu Laoer, were all injured by the explosion. Blood flowed like a river, and they fell to the ground in extreme pain. The shop owner hired a doctor to treat them, and it is said that their injuries are quite serious, and there may be danger to their lives.

Hangzhou: Xu Qinwen Case Retrial Judgment

The Xu Qinwen case, involving the Liutao tragedy at the West Lake Art School, was suspected of endangering the Republic of China. The Zhejiang High Court sentenced him to three years and six months of imprisonment. The Supreme Court found that there were doubts and sent it back for retrial. The High Court had held one hearing. The judgment was announced on the morning of the 22nd. The main text of the judgment was: Xu Qinwen knowingly concealed the fact that he was a traitor and did not report him, so he was given a reduced sentence of two years of imprisonment with a three-year suspended sentence.
