Municipal Health Bureau Convened Advertising Conference with Newspapers Yesterday; Resolved Several Measures to Regulate Medical and Pharmaceutical Advertising 121

In order to regulate medical and pharmaceutical advertising in the city's newspapers, the Municipal Health Bureau convened representatives from the advertising departments of various newspapers and representatives from various bureaus affiliated with the municipal government at the Municipal Central District Health Bureau conference room at 2 p.m. yesterday to discuss methods for regulating newspaper advertising. Chen Kecheng, representing the municipal government, Sun Yucai, representing the education bureau, Chen Lengseng, representing the social bureau, Xu Xinyi, representing the Daily Newspaper Association, Yao Zichu, representing Shen Bao, Wang Weizhen, representing Xinwen Bao, Wang Yimin, representing Shishi Xin Bao, Zeng Manjun, representing Shi Bao, Yuan Yikuang, representing Min Bao, Sun Daosheng, representing Chen Bao, Yang Kemin, representing Da Wan Bao, and Wang Hua, representing Zhonghua Ri Bao, attended. The meeting was chaired by Li Tingan, director of the Health Bureau. The following resolutions were reached: (1) Newspapers will automatically inspect and suppress previously stipulated advertisements that are not allowed to be published; (2) Questionable advertisements will be sent to the Social Bureau or the Health Bureau for review; (3) If a prohibited advertisement has been published once, the Health Bureau will notify them to avoid publishing it; (4) After the competent authority instructs Newspaper A not to publish a certain advertisement, the newspaper can notify other newspapers to avoid publishing it. The meeting adjourned at 4 p.m. It is heard that the Health Bureau is now drafting detailed rules for medical and pharmaceutical advertisements that are not allowed to be published and will send them to various newspapers as a basis.

Fuyuan Steamer Creates New Record on Sichuan River Route; Only Takes Four and a Half Days from Chongqing to Shanghai 123

The Fuyuan steamer of the Jufu Foreign Firm is the oldest ship sailing on the Sichuan River route. The hull is strong, stable, and fast. Since its maiden voyage more than ten years ago, it has been very safe. Its comfortable cabins, affordable fares, complete facilities, and attentive service are especially praised by passengers. The steamer's itinerary usually stops at Hanwan to load and unload cargo, taking nine and a half days to travel upstream from Shanghai to Chongqing and five and a half days to travel downstream from Chongqing to Shanghai. However, it departed from Chongqing at dawn on the 18th this time. Because it did not unload cargo along the way, it arrived in Shanghai at noon on the 22nd, taking only four and a half days. Its safety and speed are truly rare and it is indeed a new record for navigation on the Sichuan River route.

Two Coroner's Inquests Recorded Together 124

Guo Wang, a woman from Yancheng, residing in a straw shed in Xiaoshadu, was 52 years old. She had a son named Kai Tai, who worked as a laborer and married a woman named Wang. The family of several could manage to make a living. However, Guo Wang was plagued by illness and repeated medical treatments were ineffective. She resented her prolonged illness, spent her days sighing in frustration, and developed a desire to end her life. She attempted suicide three times, but each time she was discovered and rescued, escaping death. On the afternoon of the day before yesterday, around 2 PM, taking advantage of the fact that her son and daughter-in-law were out working and no one was around, believing the opportunity had arrived, she hanged herself with a rope from a bamboo pole behind the straw shed. When her son and daughter-in-law returned home after work and saw her, she was already cold as ice and beyond saving. The matter was discovered by the local police station. Fearing there might be other circumstances, they instructed the local security officer, Dong Xiqing, yesterday morning to report to the local court and request a coroner's inquest. Also, Du Maochang, a partner in the Hongxing Pig Business in Yangjing Town, Pudong, a native of Nanhui, recently suffered some unknown shock. On the night before last, he suddenly committed suicide by taking poison in his residence next to the fire brigade on Dingshui Road, north of Yangjing Road. Yesterday morning, his roommates discovered that Du had died and found a note of grievance on his body. They reported this to the police officer on duty, who took the note back to the Yangjing Police Station and ordered Zhuang Hongkui, the local security officer of the 24th Bao, 20th Tu, to report to the court for an inquest. For both of these cases, Prosecutor Du Jiasheng, commissioned by the court, along with Inspector Shen Qixiu, went to conduct the inquests in the afternoon.

Central Bank Inspection Report 125

The 240th inspection report on the issue reserve of Central Bank convertible notes states: "In accordance with Article 13 of the Central Bank Law, this committee is responsible for inspecting the amount of convertible notes issued by the bank and the reserve funds. The 240th inspection was held on July 20, 1935, at the Issuing Bureau of the bank. The results of the inspection are reported as follows: (A) Total amount of convertible notes issued: 10,464,3459 silver dollars, including: silver dollar notes: 9,771,5917 silver dollars, subsidiary coin notes: 6,927,542 silver dollars. Total amount of convertible note reserve: 10,464,3459 silver dollars, including: cash reserve: 8,126,3459 silver dollars. This cash reserve includes: 7,655,0616 silver dollars stored in the bank's issuing vault, 2,235,462 silver dollars deposited in branch banks in various ports, 2,477,381 silver dollars deposited with fellow banks, and a guarantee reserve equivalent to 23,380,000 silver dollars. (B) Total amount of Customs Gold Unit convertible notes issued: 373,324.70 Customs Gold Units. Total amount of Customs Gold Unit convertible note reserve: 373,324.70 Customs Gold Units. This reserve includes: 7,351.95 taels of bar gold, valued at 50779, equivalent to 373,324.70 Customs Gold Units. According to Article 22 of the Central Bank Law, the cash reserve should be at least 60%, with the remainder being a guarantee reserve consisting of legally acceptable securities. The results of this inspection show that the cash reserve exceeds 60%, and the guarantee reserve is within 40%, which is in compliance with the law. This report is hereby submitted. July 22, 1935. Chairman of the Supervisory Committee of the Central Bank, Li Fuxun, Supervisors Xie Mengjun, Bei Songsun, Qin Runqing, Yu Qiaqing, Lin Kanghou, Xu Jilun."

Weather Report 133

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated: Shandong Province: Overcast skies, brisk northeasterly to southeasterly winds. Middle reaches of the Yangtze River: Overcast skies turning clear and hot, with light northeasterly winds. Lower reaches of the Yangtze River: Skies changing from overcast to cloudy, with showers and slight easterly gales. Wenzhou coast and the East Sea: Cyclones and showers, with strong gales, caused by a hurricane moving northwest by west or west-northwest. Another hurricane south of Guam is moving west-northwest. At noon today, the center of the hurricane reached within about 60 miles of 27 degrees north latitude and 123 degrees east longitude, with severe winds. Also, in the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the highest temperature in the city was 91.9 degrees and the lowest was 77.5 degrees. On the same day last year, the highest was 84.2 degrees and the lowest was 75.9 degrees.

Aeronautical Swimming Competition Sponsored by the Aviation Association and the Liangjiang Swimming Association to be Held at the Liangjiang Women's Physical Education School on the 27th

The Shanghai Liangjiang Swimming Association held a meeting regarding the aeronautical swimming competition at 2:00 PM yesterday. Attendees included Lu Lihua, Zhang Yuliang, Ling Xitao, and Zhang Yuansheng. Lu Lihua chaired the meeting, and Zhang Yuliang recorded the minutes. The following matters were decided: (1) Regarding the proposal to appoint the officials of the competition, it was resolved to invite Wang Xiaolai to serve as the president of the Swimming Association, Lu Lihua, Yao Xijiu, and Li Dachao to serve as vice presidents, Ling Xitao to serve as the competition director, Zhang Yuansheng to serve as the general affairs director, Zhang Yuliang to serve as the publicity director, Ling Xitao to concurrently serve as the chief referee, Li Feiyun, Tan Tianpei, and Chen Fuzhang to serve as the finishing referees, Peng Sanmei, Chen Yuehe, and Li Feiyun to serve as the diving referees, Shen Guoquan to serve as the chief timekeeper, Peng Wenbao and Chen Yuehe to serve as the timekeepers, Peng Sanmei to serve as the starter, Chen Bingde and Yu Binqi to serve as the inspectors, and Hu Zongfan to serve as the recorder. The reporter and recorder will be temporarily decided by Liangjiang. (2) Regarding maintaining order at the venue, it was resolved to entrust the Liangjiang Boy Scouts. (3) Regarding how to invite athletes, it was resolved to send letters to the Southeast Women's Physical Education School, the Dongya Physical Education College, the Municipal Council Girls' High School, the Youth Team, the Guangdong Team, and the two Misses Mei and Lu to solicit participants. In addition, a registration point will be set up at the Liang Qingnianhui on Sichuan Road, Baxianqiao, so that those interested can participate separately. (4) Regarding the proposal to decide on the date of the event, it was resolved to set it for 4:00 PM on Saturday, July 27th. (5) Regarding determining the ticket price, it was resolved to divide it into special and ordinary tickets. Special tickets will be sold for one yuan each, and ordinary tickets will be sold for forty cents each. (6) Regarding determining the events, it was resolved that the men's group will have 50-meter and 100-meter freestyle, 100-meter backstroke, 200-meter breaststroke, 400-meter freestyle, and diving. The women's group will have 50-meter freestyle, 100-meter backstroke, and 200-meter breaststroke. The children's group will be the same as the women's group, plus a 150-meter three-style relay swimming (men's 50M freestyle, women's 50M backstroke, children's 50M breaststroke). (7) The draft regulations were approved. (8) Regarding how to publicize the event, it was resolved to publish advertisements on the 26th and 27th before the event, in addition to issuing news releases. (7) Regarding how to promote ticket sales, it was resolved that, in addition to the Association and Liangjiang selling a portion, the Liang Qingnianhui on Sichuan Road, Baxianqiao, will also be asked to sell them.

Competition Regulations for the Aeronautical Swimming Competition Sponsored by the Chinese Aviation Association and the Shanghai Liangjiang Swimming Association. (1) Name: Shanghai Aeronautical Swimming Competition. (2) Purpose: The purpose of this association is to increase public interest, promote swimming, and sponsor donations for aviation. (3) Date: July 27th, starting at 4:00 PM. (4) Location: Liangjiang Women's Physical Education Teachers College Swimming Pool, Xiangyin Road, Jiangwan. (5) Registration: A. Location: Both Qingnianhuis on Baxianqiao and Sichuan Road. B. Time: From the 23rd to 6:00 PM on the 25th. (6) Groups: Divided into men's group, women's group, and children's group (under 14 years old). (7) Events (Men's Group): 1. 50 meters, 2. 100-meter freestyle, 3. 100-meter backstroke, 4. 200-meter breaststroke, 5. 400-meter freestyle, 6. Diving. (Women's Group): 1. 50-meter freestyle, 2. 100-meter backstroke, 3. 100-meter breaststroke. The children's group is the same as the women's group, plus a 150-meter three-style relay swimming (men's 50M freestyle, women's 50M breaststroke, children's 50M backstroke). (8) Number of Winners: The top three in each event in each group will be selected (first place: 4 points, second place: 2 points, third place: 1 point). (9) Awards: The top three in each event will be awarded honorary certificates. The person with the most points will be awarded an additional prize.

Severing Boys and Girls Schools in Beijing 142

Social Bureau Regulates Transfer Procedures for Female Students

Since Beijing has rigorously implemented the separation of boys' and girls' schools in middle schools, the Social Bureau has been actively preparing to establish the Second Girls' Middle School and expand the First Girls' Middle School to accommodate female students from private co-educational middle schools. In addition to ordering each private middle school to report the list of female students currently in the second and third grades of junior and senior high school in each school to serve as a basis for arrangement, the bureau also took into consideration that very few names were being sent from the private schools to the bureau, and for the convenience of each female student's studies. It is specifically stipulated that each student may submit documents sufficient to prove their academic status (it is reported that documents such as student ID cards, transcripts, and notices can be used), as well as two 4-inch photos of themselves, to the bureau from the 24th of this month to the 15th of August to apply for registration. Those who have been reviewed by the bureau and found to be on file will be arranged in order. Such strict regulations will eliminate the abuse of power. After completing this registration, students no longer need to register with the school, which can save the cost of registration. Furthermore, in the future, transferring schools will be much more convenient than applying on their own. In addition, the bureau also stipulates that female students who should be entering the first grade of senior or junior high school should go directly to private girls' middle schools in the city to register according to the school's registration date. The Social Bureau's announcement and the locations of various municipal private girls' middle schools in this city are recorded below to guide the studies and further education of each female student.

Detailed Record of the Annual Meeting of the China Vocational Education Society 145

The 15th Annual Meeting of the Vocational Education Society is Held at the Same Time

Chairman Wang Zhengting Reports; Chu Minyi Delivers a Speech

(Qingdao Correspondence) The 15th Annual Meeting of the China Vocational Education Society and the 13th National Vocational Education Discussion Meeting were held simultaneously at 9 a.m. on the 19th of this month in the auditorium of the Municipal Girls' Middle School on Taiping Road in this city. A total of 206 male and female members from various provinces and cities attended the meeting. Chairman Wang Zhengyan gave an opening speech. The meeting lasted for three days. The detailed situation is recorded below:

Grand Opening Scene Around 9 a.m. on this day, all male and female members arrived on time. The guests who attended included Chu Minyi, Secretary-General of the Executive Yuan; Gu Shusen, representative of the Ministry of Education; He Siyuan, representative of the Shandong Provincial Government; Mayor Shen Honglie; Hu Jiafeng, Secretary-General of the Municipal Government; Chu Zhen, Director of the Social Bureau; Lei Fazhang, Director of the Education Bureau; Ge Futing, Chairman of the Jiaoji Railway Committee; Committee Member Lu Bianneng; and reporters from newspapers, totaling more than 206 people. After the ceremony began, Chairman Wang Zhengting gave an opening speech, followed by a speech by Secretary-General Chu. Then, Jiang Hengyuan of the Presidium reported, followed by speeches by Gu Shusen, representative of the Ministry of Education, Mayor Shen Honglie, and He Siyuan, representative of the Shandong Provincial Government. After the speeches, Huang Yanpei of the Presidium gave a reply. The ceremony was completed, and it was already past 11 a.m. The meeting was adjourned, and the meeting continued at 2 p.m. to discuss various proposals.

Chairman's Opening Speech Chairman Wang Zhengting said briefly that today is the opening of the 15th Annual Meeting of the China Vocational Education Society, and the 13th National Vocational Education Conference is being held at the same time. It is a rare opportunity for colleagues from all over the world to study and discuss with each other. First of all, we should thank Mayor Shen and the gentlemen who are in charge of the preparations here, as well as the many comrades who have warmly supported us. The reason why this year's annual meeting was decided to be held here is that Qingdao has made progress in local construction and the climate is cool. At the same time, vocational education is very developed in all aspects, which can provide us with a lot of observation and reference. This is very memorable. We have carefully reviewed the past education, and there are two major mistakes: one is from top to bottom, and the goal is to pay attention to universities, from universities to middle schools to primary schools, and to neglect primary school education. We must know that the foundation of a country lies in primary schools. Taking Russia as an example, how its political economy and other facilities are is another issue, but its efforts in general education are admirable. Sixteen years ago, illiteracy accounted for eight-tenths of the population. After the joint efforts of the people and the government, the number of illiterate people has now been reduced to two-tenths. In the future, we must promote the work of popularizing education from the lower levels to the upper levels. This kind of foundation is very important. The second is to focus on using the brain and ignore using the hands. The hands and brain cannot be unified and cannot be given equal importance. This is a major mistake. In the future, we should try to correct this shortcoming and pay attention to implementation, especially in physics and chemistry. Education must rely on government assistance and promotion. All vocational education societies must pay attention to the above two points, and under the guidance of the government, work together to promote and complete them.

Chu Minyi's Speech I came to Qingdao with President Wang, and it happened to be the annual meeting of the Vocational Education Society. I am very honored to be invited to participate. In recent years, the importance of vocational education has been gradually recognized by the Chinese people and promoted. After careful examination, education has no distinction between vocational and non-vocational. Whether it is liberal arts, science, philosophy, etc., they all contain the meaning of occupation. However, because people later paid too much attention to ideals and neglected the application of their hands, the source of this neglect has been around for a long time. Since the saying that those who labor with their minds govern others, and those who labour with their strength are governed by others, all occupations have been neglected. It must be known that in ancient times, there were no saints greater than Shennong and the Yellow Emperor. Both of them founded their countries on agriculture and industry, and they themselves were farmers and workers. Therefore, they were able to create everything and do great things. Nowadays, once you enter school, you are afraid of labour. Some people even think that studying is a way to get promoted. This is a big mistake. Even the current liberal arts, engineering, science, and medical subjects are mostly not what they have learned. And their level is stipulated to be above high school. Therefore, there are very few of these schools that belong to the United Industry. In the future, we should pay attention to establishing and promoting secondary vocational schools, and pay more attention to adapting to the environment and local conditions to avoid the blame of building cars behind closed doors. At present, the country's annual trade deficit is very large, and food, clothing, housing, and transportation all depend on foreigners. There are many dangers. How to increase production in the future should be paid special attention to. The results of your research and discussion on the improvement of vocational education will be discussed with the government, hoping that the government will adopt them and that vocational development and production will increase in the shortest possible time. The future is unlimited.

Jiang Hengyuan Reports There are about 500 members at this year's annual meeting. Due to the North China Incident and other reasons, as of now, there are 206 people who have registered, covering five cities and ten provinces. They have come from afar, from Guizhou in the south to Liaoning in the north, which makes people feel more courageous. The preparations have been enthusiastically supported by all sectors of Qingdao, which has taken a lot of effort. I am deeply grateful. Regarding the Society's undertakings, it can be divided into internal and external parts for a brief report. The Society focuses on research, and the investigation and editing items belong to it. Outside the Society is the experimental undertaking, and there are currently 30 affiliated institutions that are carrying out management. It is divided into three types: self-management, agency management, and cooperation. There are four categories of undertakings: (1) vocational school education; (2) vocational training education; (3) vocational guidance, etc.; (4) rural improvement. The future direction of efforts and advocacy can be divided into five points: (1) vocational school education, vocational training education, and vocational guidance should be developed equally; (2) for schools that have been established, the content of the school should be enriched and the way out for students should be broadened. For schools that have not been established, attention should be paid to adapting to social needs; (3) rural education should have a comprehensive rural improvement plan; (4) implement and promote women's domestic education; (5) pay attention to civic education, moral influence, especially pay attention to youth training. There are many proposals submitted by members this time, and there are also central issues for discussion. It is hoped that everyone will express their opinions as much as possible during the meeting.

Gu Shusen's Speech I originally attended the annual meeting as a member, but I was ordered by Minister Wang to represent the Ministry of Education to deliver a speech. Now, I will give a brief report on the Ministry of Education's past facilities for vocational education, the recent situation, and future plans. In 1933, the Ministry of Education investigated education in various provinces and found that there were too many middle schools and normal schools, and vocational schools accounted for less than one-tenth of the budget. Therefore, it was stipulated that the budget for middle schools should account for 40%, normal schools should account for 25%, and vocational schools should not be less than 35%. It is stipulated that this standard will be reached before 1937. Now, we are first seeking improvement in quality, not only seeking promotion in quantity, and hope to gradually achieve it. In 1932 and 1933, the Ministry promulgated two important regulations: (1) the Vocational School Law; (2) the Vocational School Regulations. Regarding the current program of vocational schools, there are several major revisions, such as internships and summer vacations, senior vocational schools are not limited to three years, and subjects can be established according to local needs. The Ministry of Education has made great efforts to promote and promote vocational education. From the spring of last year to the summer of this year, specialists have been sent to 15 provinces and cities to investigate vocational schools in great detail. The excellent ones are rewarded, and the slightly worse ones are guided and improved. The rewards are not only in writing, but also in material terms, that is, financial assistance. Special attention is paid to the difficulties of private vocational schools. Starting from 1935, it was decided to allocate special funds for application. More attention should be paid to vocational guidance, and specialists have been appointed in various provinces and cities to be responsible for promotion. Vocational guidance books have been published one after another, and will continue to be carried out in the future. Recently, the Ministry of Education plans to establish large-scale and very complete vocational schools in major cities in various provinces as models for general vocational schools. There will be at least one school in each province, and funds are being sought. In addition, special attention must be paid to production education, and more attention should be paid to production training for primary school students. Each primary school student is required to do a few production things. If each student can only produce one or half a yuan per year, the total number in the country is considerable. This is roughly the recent situation and future plans of the Ministry of Education for running vocational education.

First General Assembly The first general assembly was held at 2 p.m. the day after tomorrow, and all members attended. The report and the approved proposals are recorded below: (1) Report: A. 14 items that are requested to be adopted and implemented by the Ministry of Education; B. 7 items that are requested to be sent to the provincial and municipal governments and education departments for selection and implementation; C. 15 items to be handled by the Society; D. 2 items related to Society affairs; (2) Explanation: A. and B. (omitted) C. This year's annual meeting received 51 proposals from all parties and one paper. 13 proposals were reserved, and the remaining 38 proposals were classified as follows: 14 related to administration, 7 related to vocational schools, 3 related to vocational courses, 6 related to continuing education and vocational guidance, 7 related to rural improvement, and 1 other miscellaneous item. After classification, they will be discussed in groups. C (omitted) (3) Future Efforts: A. Enrichment of vocational school education; B. Promotion of vocational continuing education; C. Practical implementation of vocational guidance; D. Improvement of the countryside; E. Implementation of women's home economics education. Based on these nine major policies, practical work is the focus of consistent efforts by colleagues in the future.

Results of the Middle School Normal School Graduation Joint Examination Announced in This City 148

The Shanghai Middle School and Physical Education Normal School Graduation Joint Examination for this year was held on the 24th, 25th, and 26th of last month for three days. The results were satisfactory and all results have been announced yesterday. According to statistics, the number of schools participating in the joint examination was 65 high schools, 89 junior high schools, and 5 physical education normal schools, for a total of 159 schools. The number of students participating in the joint examination was 1,870 high school students, 2,726 junior high school students, and 134 physical education normal school students. There were 144 high school make-up examinees and 80 junior high school make-up examinees, for a total of 4,954 people. As a result of the joint examination, 1,434 out of 1,870 high school students passed and were approved to graduate, accounting for 76.7%. 363 had to make up exams, 61 were held back, and 12 did not finish the exam. 2,224 out of 2,726 junior high school students passed and were approved to graduate, accounting for 81.5%. 434 had to make up exams, 59 were held back, and 9 did not finish the exam. 120 out of 134 physical education normal school students passed and were approved to graduate, accounting for 94.7%. 11 had to make up exams, 2 were held back, and 1 did not finish the exam. There were 8 award-winning high school students and 22 award-winning junior high school students, for a total of 30 people. Furthermore, the average number of students in each school who took the joint examination was 80 points for Zhengshi Middle School in the high school division, 76 points for Huizhong Middle School in the junior high school division, and 76 points for the Chinese Women's Physical Education Normal School in the physical education normal school division.

As for the students who should have participated in the joint examination this year, some were absent due to illness or other reasons, and some did not finish the exam. The schools should submit a request for leave, which is understandable. After deliberation by the Joint Examination Committee, it was decided to allow them to participate in the next joint examination to make up for it. However, the schools must still register and handle the matter to complete the procedures. Instructions have been issued to each school to comply with them.

The Annual Meeting of the Chinese Economic Society is Rescheduled to Be Held in Guangzhou Starting on December 26th 149

The Chinese Economic Society was scheduled to hold its 12th Annual Meeting in Guangzhou starting on August 28th this year, as previously reported. It is now known that the Society recently received requests from a majority of members, who felt that it would be hot in Guangzhou at that time, and that the meeting was approaching soon, making it difficult to have enough time to prepare papers and to write them carefully, which would affect the number of attendees. Therefore, they unanimously advocated postponing the meeting. Yesterday, the Society specifically convened its 11th Council meeting to discuss the matter and agreed that the majority opinion should be followed. It was decided to reschedule the annual meeting to be held from December 26th to 29th this year, still in Guangzhou. This is because the members of the Society are either tied up with their duties or are university professors, and at that time, they can take advantage of the year-end vacation to gather in the famous city and discuss together.

Establishment of the Municipal Drama Research Association for the Revival of Spoken Drama Movement 151

Urgently Seeking to Improve Scripts and Train Talents, with Chen Dabe and Wang Zhongxian Taking Charge

The Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Education considers drama to be the most authoritative tool for promoting social education. Therefore, starting in 1933, Ding Shouye of the Bureau's Opera and Recording Review Committee was responsible for leading the city's entertainment circles to organize research associations separately, to seek improvements and achieve practical results. So far, the officially established associations include the Shanghai Comic Monologue Research Association, the Shanghai Shenqu Opera Research Association, the Shanghai Sutang Opera Research Association, the Shanghai Yongyu Society's Shanghai Storytelling Research Association, the Shanghai Siming Opera Research Association, and the Shanghai Pingci Pinghua Research Association, totaling more than ten groups. The Shanghai Spoken Drama Research Association held its inaugural meeting at the Municipal Public Education Center on Wenmiao Road at 10:00 AM yesterday. Director Pan of the Education Bureau originally intended to attend in person, but due to temporary official business, he sent Section Chief Jiang Jianbai to attend instead. Details are recorded as follows:

More than 250 members attended the inaugural meeting, including Chen Dabe, Wang Zhongxian, Li Junpan, and Hu Hensheng. Huang Tiwen, representative of the Municipal Party Department, Jiang Jianbai, representative of the Education Bureau, and Ding Shoutang of the Opera and Recording Review Committee attended to provide guidance. The presidium consisted of Chen Dabe, Wang Zhongxian, Xu Zhuodai, Li Junpan, Hu Hensheng, Chen Wuwo, and Xu Hanmei. After formal salutations, Chairman Hu Hensheng reported on the preparatory process, followed by speeches by Huang Tiwen, representative of the Municipal Party Department, and Jiang Jianbai, representative of the Education Bureau. Ding Shoutang and Chen Dabe also delivered speeches. Subsequently, the charter was approved, proposals were discussed, and directors and supervisors were elected. The meeting adjourned without taking a group photo.

In his speech, Huang Tiwen, representative of the Municipal Party Department, stated that spoken drama groups are organizations that promote culture and social education. The spoken drama movement was once popular in the early Republic of China and was regarded as a new product of China, and was quite popular with the society. However, it gradually declined due to a lack of organization. Now that the Spoken Drama Research Association has been established, it should strive to research and improve in order to seek development. In his speech, Section Chief Jiang of the Education Bureau stated that there are many types of drama, but spoken drama has the greatest value. Unlike many other dramas whose wording is too deep or limited to locality, and cannot be understood by the public, its impact on society is therefore very large. He hoped that everyone can sincerely research and receptively accept the opinions of others so that spoken drama can develop. Regarding the source of materials, first, it must have a national spirit, and second, it must have a creative spirit. In his speech, Ding Shoutang expressed the hope that the materials for reforming dramas could be improved, and to cultivate one's own personality. In his speech, Chen Dabe expressed the hope that people in the spoken drama circles can be aware and clearly understand that spoken drama is not only for entertainment, but also has the significance of educating the people.

Discussion of Proposals: (1) Approval of the association charter; (2) All members shall pay a monthly contribution of 2%. Those who do not report will be penalized double once discovered; (3) Within five years, all groups are not allowed to recruit students. If recruitment is necessary, each person shall pay one hundred yuan to subsidize the association fee and be approved by the association for recruitment and training, and then introduced to various groups; (4) From now on, the stage scripts of all groups should be unified; (5) Those who perform spring dramas and Taoist dramas are allowed to join this association.

Elected Directors and Supervisors: Chen Dabe, Hu Hensheng, Gu Jianqiu, Xu Hanmei, Wu Yixiao, Zhu Yu'er, Li Zhuan, Wang Raoyou, Wang Tiexue, Wang Moto, Fang Tie Mei, Qin Zilong, Chen Wuwo, Wang Shaobai, Jiang Daier, and fifteen others were elected as directors. Zhang Siwei, Xu Limin, Gu Ya'er, Li Junzhi, Tang Wuseng, and five others were elected as alternate directors. Li Junpan, Qin Haha, Song Chiseng, Zhang Ye'er, Zhou Tianbei, Zhao Jingzhong, Dong Biesheng, and seven others were elected as supervisors. Yu Tiehun, Zhu Yizhen, Miao Yiyun, and three others were elected as alternate supervisors.

Finance: Big Players Covering Shorts, Spot Gold Weakens then Recovers Strongly 154

Although Indian Silver Rises, Trading Becomes Quiet; Resulting in a Rebound of 3.4 Yuan

The gold market initially fell yesterday due to selling spurred by foreign telegram news, but unexpectedly, big players suddenly covered shorts, causing a sharp rebound. Although Indian silver later rose, the trading became quiet and sentiment became firm, resulting in a rebound. In the morning, it was reported that foreign silver markets were stable, with the forward silver price in Monterrey unchanged or up 1.4 cents. Exchange rates all rose, and London spot gold remained unchanged. Sentiment was still weak, and off-exchange trading opened at 51.2 yuan, with sellers plentiful. It soon fell into the 50 yuan range. The Central Bank announced its listing, with the British pound unchanged and the US dollar rising. The customs gold unit remained unchanged, and the spot gold standard price was listed at 869.6 yuan, with little impact. The morning opened low, and after the opening, sellers were abundant. The Associated Press reported that Senator McCarran, a silver advocate, said that the tax on profits from the sale of Japanese silver might be abolished. A private telegram from the New Feng Yang Company also said that the Ministry of Finance had sent personnel to conduct on-site investigations, and the price gradually fell. Banks seized the opportunity to buy on the cheap. The Hong Kong and Shanghai Banking Corporation also listed the British pound and the US dollar as equal, and buyers took advantage of the low prices to remain active, which helped to maintain the price. Later, big players suddenly came to cover shorts, rising to outside the 50 yuan range. At this time, with the Hong Kong market opening firm at .0625, there was still a chance to make a profit. However, Yuan Mao Yong repeatedly purchased heavily, and sellers were helpless. The exchange rate was also tight, and Hengxing also came to cover shorts, gradually rising the price. However, because there were also many who supplied at the high price, there were many trades after the rise. In the end, the forecast for Indian silver rose by 5 annas, but because the chips in the trading market were relatively scarce, the general trend showed a range-bound trading pattern, lacking special changes, and fluctuating. The afternoon market opened steadily, and then buying interest rebounded. The trading market was originally scarce, and the price gradually rose. Spring and Autumn

Tidbits 166

—(Microorganism)

Watches and clocks, made on the same machine, with the same model number, style, and brand, sold from the same watch factory, can still be "fast or slow," accurate or inaccurate, just like people who come out of the same "mother's womb," with the same seven orifices, five senses, and bodies, but with differences in "intelligence" and "good and evil."

If a person in charge can first "discard" themselves, then whatever they do will not cause enmity or resentment, and they can do it perfectly and successfully. Furthermore, they should think in reverse: always make sure that if I ask someone to "swallow this iron bullet," I can also "earn it down" myself.

One pair of hands can only block out one sun. This is a wonderful metaphor for "those who engage in infighting." Large institutions, companies, and branches have dozens to hundreds of employees. One person only has one pair of hands and can only hold one position. How can they be like the Thousand-Hand Guanyin, using multiple hands to perform tasks? If you "squeeze out colleagues like maggots" and have all the positions "done by you" and all the salaries "taken by you," it would probably be impossible in reality!

A Special Account of the Maiden Voyage of the Da Da 167

— Jiping

These past few days have been truly stifling. Living in the bustling city and leading a weary life, I often think of going to the countryside to admire the emerald green fields and breathe in the fresh air. However, burdened by labor and commitments, how can you be carefree? Yesterday happened to be a Sunday, and Dr. Jianqiu and Mr. and Mrs. Yeyu came to visit. After chatting happily for a while, we decided to take a half-day trip. Some suggested bathing at the beach to benefit the body and mind, while others suggested a picnic in the park for a special flavor. I opened the Shen Bao, wanting to find a special place to go, and suddenly saw the news that the Da Da new ship was inviting guests for a maiden voyage to Wusong. Enjoying the cool breeze of the Huangpu River was just the way to escape the heat, so we finally reached a unanimous agreement. Immediately after lunch, we took a car to the Da Da pier to board.

The Da Da was built by the Great China Shipyard. Its exterior is very beautiful, and its interior is very luxurious. In less than an hour, over a thousand guests crowded out of the city, presumably expressing sympathy with us. At that moment, the ship was unmoored, and the crowd cheered. Music and explosions echoed each other, shaking the air of the 16th Pier! As the ship left Yangshupu, the hosts treated the guests with soda, beer, and refreshments, being extremely courteous. As we ate, we admired the scenery on both sides of the Huangpu River. Having not been to the countryside for a long time, we felt an extraordinary appreciation for the loveliness of the countryside. The ship sailed about ten miles out of Songkou, then turned back along the original route, taking three and a half hours, breaking the estimated four-hour record. During the return trip, we visited all parts of the ship and were deeply impressed by the scientific equipment and management implemented by Da Da, truly the crown of domestic river ships.

On the ship, we met General Manager Zhang Xiaoruo, who told us that Da Da Company has been striving for prosperity for thirty years, rising from setbacks and resurgence. He felt the difficulty of starting a business and the challenges of improvement. At a time when the domestic economy is in a panic, he built this new ship with a huge investment of 500,000 yuan, hoping to fulfill his long-cherished wish to continue the past and open up the future. Listening to his words reminded me of the former sage of Tonghai, Zhang Qian, who strongly advocated utilizing resources to benefit the people, creating industries, developing education, opening transportation, and organizing charitable deeds. His great spirit and achievements indeed made later generations feel solemn respect! How many people like Zhang Qian can be found in today's world?

Seasonal Occupations 168

— Zhuying

In cities plagued by economic recession, making a living seems not to be an easy task, especially for small businesses that feel the difficulties. However, my neighbor Old Man Wei is an exception.

Old Man Wei is nearly fifty years old this year and in very good spirits. He says that my strong body is my asset. Three hundred and sixty-five days a year, he gets up at dawn every day. He doesn't have a fixed job. His job changes with the seasons. These days, he is peddling cold drinks suitable for this season, such as sour plum soup for two cents a cup, and sometimes ice cream or shaved ice for three cents a cup. Sliced watermelon is also naturally what he sells every year. Although these things are frowned upon by hygienists, he relies on them to get through the whole summer.

When the weather cools down, he sells "Suzhou Tender Lotus Root," or "White Lily," or "Water Chestnut." Sometimes, if he has more capital, he sells "Dazha Crabs." In short, he sells whatever has the highest profit margin. In winter, he always sells "Roasted Sweet Potatoes" at the alley entrance. In early spring, there is really nothing to sell, so he sells green vegetables. But in late spring, he sells small yellow croaker fish, or goes to the countryside to get willow branches and peach blossoms to sell and make money. And he is not willing to let go of the festivals such as the Dragon Boat Festival, Mid-Autumn Festival, and New Year.

His son, A Da, sells glutinous rice rolls. But besides selling glutinous rice rolls, he also sells zongzi in the spring, warm lotus root in the autumn, and glutinous rice balls in rice wine in the winter. In the summer, as usual, he gets rid of the glutinous rice roll bucket and turns it into a cold noodle stall, selling jelly and cold mung bean soup.

Although the father and son each have their own household and bear the burden of their families, their lives are quite comfortable.

Mummy 169

— (Wang Letian)

The West Lake Museum in Hangzhou recently displayed a mummy, attracting crowds of men, women, old, and young from Hangzhou to visit. Boatmen and rickshaw pullers have also changed their slogans, immediately saying to customers: "Sir! Going to see the mummy?"

I arrived in Hangzhou and happened to encounter this event, so I hired a boat with my older brother Mutian to go see it. Upon landing, we immediately saw that the inside and outside of the museum gate were extremely crowded. After signing our names, we proceeded to the room displaying animals. Before entering, we saw a display case surrounded by spectators, which contained the so-called mummy. The case was divided into two compartments. The upper compartment displayed the mummy's head, padded with absorbent cotton. We could see that the facial features had decomposed, and the back of the head had a hair bun with a gold hairpin inserted. Upon closer inspection, it was an old woman. The skull was ash-black in color, and its texture did not resemble human bone but rather mineral matter. Within the right eye socket, we vaguely saw what appeared to be an eyeball, no different from a dead fish's eye. The lower compartment contained a pair of the mummy's hands and feet. The feet were small, and the muscles had contracted, resembling boiled chicken or duck wings. The people of Hangzhou did not know the meaning of mummy, and rumors said that it was a zombie that had been defeated by the villagers.

Little Western Paradise 170

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter Sixteen Tears Hidden Behind Curtains, Difficult to Escape Cold Eyes, Fortunes Boasted by Garments, Once Arrived at a Powerful Door

Jiefu laughed: Not busy for the time being. These words probably stayed in Mr. Cheng's heart. Within six or seven days, brother will have a small position to announce. This is all thanks to Mr. Jia Duocai's eight-line flattery. When making friends outside, no one knows when they will be useful and when they will not, so it is always best to make as many friends as possible. For example, this Mr. Jia, I do not know him, but he was introduced by Mr. Li Shilian. However, the things that Mr. Li is trying to do do not have any news, and my things have a very good chance. Mr. Jia is extremely generous and does not lose the demeanor of a banker. In the future, when a branch bank is established in Xi'an, he will definitely be the branch manager. If Mr. Li stays in Xi'an for a longer period of time, I think there will always be a way. Zhiqian did not smoke cigarettes, so he had to learn to take a cigarette and smoke it. In this room, the noise turned into silence. Jiefu had no way to praise Mr. Jia any further. After thinking for a while, just as he was about to speak again, Miss Yang Wanhua passed by outside the window wearing a new green silk cheongsam. Jiefu immediately exclaimed, quite surprised. When Wanhua heard these words, she stood outside the window and stopped walking. Zhang Jiefu disregarded everything and quickly went out to greet her. Wanhua laughed: Mr. Zhang, I have decided to leave early tomorrow morning. What about the letter of introduction that you promised to write for me? Jiefu cupped his hands and laughed: I am really very sorry. I went to the Construction Department at six o'clock this morning. I came back for less than twenty minutes, received a call from the Finance Department, and I went to the Finance Department again. It just so happened that Chief Wang had something to do and invited the director to talk. (272)

Records of Fragrant Incense Floating Vaguely 171

— Originally written by Princess Deling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

Of course, they accused him of more serious things than these, but I can't remember many of them; however, they were generally of the same nature as these six, and it is not difficult to understand what kinds of crimes that Governor Lao committed! The first and second articles above were nothing more than accusing him of being good at exploiting the people's wealth for his own benefit, which of course was not anything particularly special; but the third article could not but make the author offer an explanation! Because in the eyes of people today, no matter who is the chairman, president, or minister, they can openly dine in restaurants and eateries in the market, which is not considered a loss of official status; but in the former Qing Dynasty, the situation was different. Generally, high-ranking officials were not accustomed to going to restaurants outside to drink and eat; needless to say, they could not go to brothels! At that time, people regarded restaurants as inferior places exclusively for ordinary people, and high-ranking officials paid particular attention to these small details, which were especially likely to attract attention; even the people who opened restaurants, if there was an official who often went to their place to eat and drink, no matter how much business he brought them, they would always discuss him first and point fingers at him. What was the reason for this? To put it bluntly, there is only one sentence. That is because these kinds of things were not common; especially because those high officials who ruled one side were in fact the representatives of the imperial court and could be said to be a part of the imperial court. They should respect themselves more and not casually rush into restaurants, causing people to look down on them. Not only would they lose their own dignity, but it would also affect the prestige of the imperial court. Therefore, this charge was obviously a very serious one! (372)

Local Customs

West Gate Past 172

— Shanghai News Agency

Shanghai News Agency has a plan to "take charge of the past of the four gates." Today, we announce that we will take charge of the West Gate.

When talking about the West Gate, we must start from outside the West Gate, even before Shanghai had a county seat; this is to say the "Huangjia Que" first.

Outside the current West Gate, there is a very famous Huangjia Guo Road. Speaking of this place, it should have been famous a long time ago. Originally, Huang Ming of the Yuan Dynasty lived here. His residence was called Xijiao Yequ Xuan, and people called him Mr. Xijiao. At that time, Shanghai did not yet have a county seat, but it had already established a county. The county government was exactly the center of the old site where the city was later built; therefore, Xijiao was equal to what was later called "outside the West Gate," and the name Huangjia Que came about precisely because Huang Ming lived in this place.

People who live near the West Gate have a convenient and picturesque place to go, just like those who live on Luban Road, North Sichuan Road, Jiaozhou Road... because they can regard the Temple of Confucius Park (i.e., the Shanghai Civic Education Center) as their own garden, just like Gujiazhai Park, Hongkou Park, Jiaozhou Park. Speaking of the Temple of Confucius, it is the former school palace. It probably has a deep connection with the West Gate. Although it moved from the East Gate to the West Gate, and then moved back again, it ended up still being in the West Gate. —In the first year of Yuanzhen (1295) of the Yuan Dynasty, the Shanghai County School was changed from a town school. It was originally in the East Gate. In the third year of Dazhi (1310), Qu Tingfa helped with the fields and moved it to the West Gate. In the first year of Yanyou (1314), County Magistrate Wang Gui moved it back to its old home. In this way, it passed through the Ming Dynasty, and then through the Qing Dynasty and the Six Dynasties. In the third year of Xianfeng (1853), on the fifth day of the eighth month, with a clap of thunder, the Small Swords Society occupied the county seat. Unlike the Manchu Qing official books that carried out anti-revolutionary propaganda, the Small Swords Society knew how to respect culture. Even though they were besieged by the Qing army and stubbornly defended the city, they were able to widely establish free schools to educate the people. On the other hand, after the Qing army gained control and entered the county seat, they burned the school palace to a crisp. After the war was pacified, the school palace was rebuilt, and this time it was located in the West Gate again. If this had not happened, the current Temple of Confucius Park would probably have given the greatest convenience to the people living in the East Gate, and we would have been chatting about it in "Taking Charge of the Past of the East Gate."

There is a Temple of Confucius inside the West Gate, which has become the center of Confucianism; outside the West Gate, there is a center of Taoism—that is, the Shanghai Baiyun Temple, with the front door on Fangxie Road and the back door on Zhaozhou Road, and the content is quite large. When it started in the eighth year of Guangxu (1882), it was originally a small Leizu Temple; after six years, it received the Taoist canon and, following the example of the Baiyun Temple in Beijing, was designated as a "Ten-Fang Jungle," and only then was the current name changed, and the scale became increasingly large.

Next to the Baiyun Temple is a famous church girls' school—the Bridgman Girls' School. Its naming is to commemorate the missionaries Bridgman and his wife. The two Bridgmams were missionaries of the American Congregational Church and came to Shanghai in the twenty-seventh year of Daoguang (1847) to preach.

Diagonally across from the Bridgman Girls' School is a famous church hospital—the Women and Children's Hospital, its original translated name is "Margaret Williamson Hospital." It was founded by the American Missionary Society missionary Luo Sinaide and was dedicated to diagnosing diseases for women and children, especially focusing on obstetrics. Ms. Williamson of New York heard about this and generously donated all of her decades of savings to this hospital. This is the reason why the Women and Children's Hospital was originally named. The Women and Children's Hospital was founded in the eleventh year of Guangxu (1885) of the Qing Dynasty, and held its 50th anniversary this year (1935) on May 11.

Arriving at the Women and Children's Hospital, if you walk a few steps east along Daji Road, you can return to Huangjia Que Road, which we mentioned at the beginning. If you go south into Shangwen Road, don't forget that it is the former Shangwen Gate (Little West Gate); if you go north into Zhaojia Road, don't forget that it is Yifeng Gate (Old West Gate). Okay, goodbye.

Free Talk

Idle Chats of Today 173

— Yi Feng

Recently, various publications often have a column called "Idle Chats and Casual Remarks." What is discussed in these columns is mostly headache-inducing material. Because of this, some people inevitably become anxious. Universities, not wanting to be left out, also start publications, also engage in "Idle Chats and Casual Remarks," also want to critique others, and quickly catch up.

Their criticisms, on the surface, still carry a bit of a gentlemanly and scholarly air. They don't seem to be openly scolding people, and their scheming is always roundabout. But clearly, after drinking and becoming tipsy, they gossip about Zhang San's strengths and Li Si's weaknesses, yet they pretend to be nonchalant, acting cultured and refined, engaging in gentle conversations and whispering, as if they have the demeanor of unrestrained scholars who dismiss everything with a laugh. Therefore, if they want to verbally attack someone, they don't show any hint of anger, because they have clearly stated that they are just chatting idly and making casual remarks. Isn't that very clear? Idle chats are unrestrained, talking about anything and everything, and casual remarks are just things that come to mind occasionally, whispering among themselves. How can anyone take it seriously? If you choose to believe it, then of course I am not responsible, because I am just expressing my feelings! That's all.

The method is cleverly deceptive, but unfortunately, the tail inevitably gets exposed in the end. For example, when they talk about how you aren't doing well and he isn't doing well either, then you have to ask who is doing well? Of course, it's only themselves. Although they don't say it explicitly, it's self-evident. The intention of the "talkers" is only this.

Secondly, their idle chats and casual remarks, because their purpose is to attack others or facts, are of course aimed at specific targets and are different from aimless rambling. Therefore, their tone and language are specifically directed at certain people. As a result, only certain people become their greatest enemies. As for bandits, thieves, and burglars, they are of no concern to them. Not only can they ignore them, but if it is beneficial to themselves, they might even collude with them for convenience. Such gentlemanly and scholarly behavior is truly breathtaking.

In the past, some people said that village gossip was not to be trusted, but now it seems that is not entirely true. Today, only the words of scholars are mostly completely false. Serious talk is not necessary to discuss, idle chats and casual remarks, have become ulterior motives. The above-mentioned kind of critique is one example.

Speaking of this, I am beginning to like village gossip. Because although it is vulgar and unsophisticated, it is still genuine, and although it is absurd, it is not concealed at all, so it is likable. But can you get even one percent of the truth from today's scholar's idle chats and casual remarks? Truly, Amen!

On "Personification" 174

— Wang Jicong

Gorky once said: "We often hear, 'The wind is crying,' 'The wind is sobbing,' 'The moon shines thoughtfully,' 'The waves want to shake the rocks. Although the rocks frown slightly at the impact of the waves, they are not defeated by the waves,' 'Boots do not want to be worn by feet,' 'Glass is sweating profusely'—even though glass has no sweat glands."

"All of this is 'personification,' which is intended to make it easier for us to understand natural phenomena. Here, we are attributing our own human characteristics to everything we see."

Natsume Soseki, in his famous "Theory of Literature," classified "personification" as "projective language" and offered the following explanation:

"In my language, the most emotional aspects should naturally be attached to the most emotional beings, ourselves. Laughter and anger, for example, are both qualified to express the essence of emotional disasters. Therefore, things written in these languages will clearly and vividly convey emotional bonds and will naturally evoke a lively state. There is no doubt about this. Moreover, when explaining the phenomena of the universe, the standard is one's own individual. Matters surrounding oneself are all drawn to this center and decided by one's own emotions. In other words, we have a tendency to readily transfer our own emotions to understand other things. I will now tentatively call this projective language, meaning the means of projecting oneself to explain the outside world. So-called personification or Prosopopoeia should all be included in this."

"There are unexpectedly many examples of this grammar in the languages we habitually use in our daily lives. For example, 'rain feet crossing the river,' 'the whispers of leaves,' 'drawer handles.' In European languages, such as 'seam eyes,' 'hinges,' are all authentic projective language."

Both Gorky and Natsume Soseki's explanations are correct, but I have one more point to add here:

The so-called "personification" is the descriptive principle used by writers in their literary works to anthropomorphize natural phenomena. Because literature conveys human thoughts and feelings through vivid imagery, using expressions that describe human life phenomena to describe certain natural phenomena, thereby linking those natural phenomena with human life phenomena and with our thoughts and feelings, will inevitably enhance the ability to convey thoughts and feelings. For example, when describing that it is getting late, writing "Night comes from the distant mountains" (although night has no feet) will certainly be more interesting than writing "It is gradually getting dark."

We know that every writer inevitably expresses certain social thoughts and feelings in their works, and their depiction of natural phenomena is merely an attempt to strengthen the thoughts and feelings they express. Therefore, a writer's use of "personification" to describe natural phenomena, like their entire creative method, is determined by the content of the thoughts and feelings they want to express; it is conveyed through their worldview, their mood; it is not merely their baseless fantasy. For example, our great poet Li Bai, he liked to use "personification" to describe nature, but his method of description is always combined with his consciousness. Now, let's just take one of his poems at random—"Drinking Alone by Moonlight"—

"A pot of wine among the flowers, I drink alone, no kith or kin. I raise my cup to invite the bright moon, Facing my shadow, we become three people. The moon does not know how to drink, My shadow merely follows my body. I temporarily accompany the moon and shadow, Enjoying pleasure while we must. I sing, and the moon lingers, I dance, and my shadow scatters. When sober, we rejoice together, When drunk, we part ways. We forever form a friendship without emotion, Promising to meet again in the distant Milky Way."

This poem not only demonstrates Li Bai's ability to appropriately and skillfully apply "personification" to describe the scene of drinking alone by moonlight, but such a depiction enhances the artistic expressiveness of his feelings of loneliness and decadence revealed in this poem. If Li Bai's feelings of loneliness and decadence, and the poetic inspiration derived from them, stemmed from the decline of the aristocracy at the time, then his use of "personification" here is also linked to the sentiments of the declining aristocracy. Because only a declining group would feel lonely and need to leave reality and the crowd, "raising a cup to invite the bright moon" to dispel their sorrow and sadness.

Another example is Guo Moruo's "Vase," which also contains many natural phenomena that the author describes using "personification," for example:

"Plum blossoms, I thank you for your subtle feelings,

You bring back my youth.

The spring in my heart, long since dried up,

Bursts forth from my petrified chest."

In fact, plum blossoms are not affectionate girls, so where do their "subtle feelings" come from? They also have no hands or feet, so how can they "bring back" anything for anyone? However, his things, or rather, everything related to his lover, is "affectionate." Guo Moruo's "Vase" is a "love poem" about the love-above-all-else ideology of decadent petty bourgeois, and the feeling of love-above-all-else can be said to fill the entire poem. The plum blossom depicted here is a gift from the poet's lover, so in the poet's feeling, the plum blossom is very "affectionate." Thus, the plum blossom is personified. Such a depiction certainly enhances the passion expressed in the poem, and also enhances the feelings of love-above-all-else expressed by the author. Therefore, we can say that the "personification" used in "Vase" was determined by the author's contemporary petty bourgeois consciousness of love-above-all-else.

In short, the so-called "personification," like the general principles of describing scenes and expressing feelings, flows from the content expressed in the work; further, it is connected with the writer's thoughts and feelings, and with his worldview. As for appropriately applying this method to describe nature, it goes without saying that one must have imagination. But a rich imagination does not come from the sky; it is composed of rich life experiences and knowledge. Therefore, in the end, to appropriately apply "personification," one must have rich life experiences and a deep understanding of general social life. Because only by having a deep understanding of life can one combine and unify natural phenomena with life, and thus be able to use "personification" to describe nature. For example, the bright moon, in the feelings of the lonely and decadent Li Bai, is a drinking companion; in the feelings of a love poet, it is a beautiful girl; in the eyes of a thief who wants to steal in the dark, it may be a very annoying person... If you do not understand the lives and moods of these people, then when describing their lives and encountering the scene of a bright moon in the sky, you will not be able to appropriately use "personification" to describe it; this is a very obvious thing.

A Drunkard (Continued) 175

— Lin Ni

Third Uncle-grandfather told stories to the children, and they all loved him. I never saw Third Uncle-grandfather read books, but he had a belly full of stories - the stories in Third Uncle-grandfather's belly could not be carried away even with fifty loads. On summer nights, after dinner, the men and children would go to the threshing ground behind the house to enjoy the cool, and the children would surround Third Uncle-grandfather, asking him to tell stories. Third Uncle-grandfather's meal was often later, and if they waited impatiently, they would publicly appoint someone to go to Third Uncle-grandfather's house to see. When Third Uncle-grandfather came, the children immediately made a fuss, "Don't make noise, I just ate, the food is still in my throat, let me smoke a bit before telling the stories." After loading the yellow tobacco, the children lit it for him, one puff, two puffs, three puffs, and the stories followed the smoke. Stories from Journey to the West, Investiture of the Gods, Wu Song fighting the tiger, Kong Ming borrowing arrows, Xue Rengui breaking through Motian Ridge, these were all the stories that the children liked to hear. Sometimes he also told stories from Strange Tales from a Chinese Studio, which they liked to hear, but they were also afraid of encountering such ghosts, and they sat there without daring to move. Someone would go back to sleep alone, deliberately coughing a few times when passing through dark places, as if someone was following behind, desperately opening their legs to run.

Third Uncle-grandfather was a porter. I never met Third Uncle-grandfather's father, but it was said that he was also a porter. Third Uncle-grandfather, at the age of fourteen or fifteen, followed his father as a porter, thus inheriting the trade. When I knew him, Third Uncle-grandfather had been a porter for many years - yes, Third Uncle-grandfather often said that he saw me born, in the year that the river embankment collapsed, in the blink of an eye, I had grown so big. Third Uncle-grandfather was not a porter all year round, and there was not always work for porters all year round. Third Uncle-grandfather also farmed, Third Uncle-grandfather also had his own fields, near the well. According to Third Uncle-grandfather, the fields were "as big as the palm of your hand," which was practically as if he had no fields. During the busy farming season, after finishing his own field work, he also did odd jobs for others. Third Uncle-grandfather was strong and nimble, and he was fast at transplanting rice seedlings and harvesting rice, one person was worth two or three women, and the families with more fields competed to hire him. But Third Uncle-grandfather's wages were also twice as much as others, and they also had to buy him liquor to drink, otherwise, the work would definitely be less.

After handing over the cargo, returning from the city, sometimes there was pork hanging on the carrying pole, but it didn't happen often in a year. Later, when I grew older, I went to the gambling house with him many times, and only when he won would he be so generous. He usually lost more often than he won. He didn't care about losing money, and he said to me, "Gambling is either winning or losing, gambling, gambling, is about 'bo.' If you're sure to win, who would gamble with you?" When he won, it was "unexpected wealth," and he bought a lot of everything. If you told him not to buy too much, he would say, "Embarrassing, embarrassing, if you want to eat, eat enough, don't be such a small dog. What's the point of not eating the money you win? Keep it to build a house? If fate decrees that you'll get rich, you'll get rich, there's no use in being frugal if you're not destined to. A person works hard just to eat, count one day at a time. You didn't bring money when you were born, and you can't take it into the grave when you die, right?"

"Gambling! Gambling! Look at Third Uncle-grandfather, didn't he even gamble away his son?" The elders would admonish their children in this way. This refers to his second son, when he was seven years old, he said he would take him to the city, and he was never seen again. It was said that it was for gambling. It was said that the child was sold to a relative in a neighboring county. Later, Third Uncle-grandfather went to see him a few times, and the child had become white and fat, and he secretly called him "Dad." Many years later, I won some money, and we both ate our fill and got drunk. On the way home from the city, we talked intermittently, pulling and tugging, and somehow we got to that matter. I asked him, "It's not like you had many, just two sons, how could you bear to sell him to someone else?" "Ah, nephew, it's like cutting my heart out, am I not human? But where would I get the ability to raise him? If he stayed in my house, he would suffer from cold and hunger, it's better to let him be sold to someone else - he'll have good food, good clothes, and be able to read books. My father was a porter, I'm a porter, do you want him to be like me too?" He answered me like this. I didn't ask again, whether he sold his son because he lost money, or he lost the money he got from selling his son, I didn't know for sure.

Baoshan, Third Uncle-grandfather's eldest son, carried water and cooked in a store in the city. One year, Shan Cai, who used to be a cook at the elementary school, became a platoon leader and returned to the county in great style to recruit soldiers. This moved Baoshan's heart, and he said that he also wanted to be a soldier. Third Uncle-grandfather looked down on it, "Anything is good, but being a soldier - being a soldier is cheaper than a dog. I raised him, but he doesn't listen to me, let him do whatever he wants. He doesn't want to be a good person, he wants to be a bad person, let him suffer and he'll know." In the end, Baoshan and three other young men from the village followed the recruiting soldiers together.

For several days, Third Uncle-grandfather was not seen, and everyone was surprised. Someone said that they had seen him carrying goods to the city that day. Half a year later, he came back, sick, very thin, and very weak. He said that he had been captured by the army to be a porter, and he took the opportunity to escape, begging all the way back.

With his cousin presiding, Uncle Quanfeng and Uncle Ruiqing witnessing, the fields near the well were sold off to take care of his funeral. On a clear autumn afternoon, Third Uncle-grandfather was placed in the middle of the coffin, carried by two people. The people who had heard him tell stories, struck gongs, scattered paper money, and sent him to the mountains. There, lay his father, his mother, and his brothers. (The End)

University Days (28) 176

— By German Storm, Translated by Chen Yin Zhi

"Late in the afternoon, we had already washed the clothes indoors, and we came to the yard, wanting to hang the clothes on the wooden stakes in the middle of the cemetery. Julie rolled up her clothes to mid-thigh, smoothed her black hair behind her ears, and carried the small wooden stool from one wooden stake to another. The old woman was dozing in the armchair; I, I am not tall, I can't help her!"

Speaking to this point, Lame Mary stood up to straighten her weak body for me to see.

"I was sitting on a big stone next to the clothes basket, watching the neighbor's coachman brush a golden chestnut horse. I have always liked horses, you know, my father was also a coachman. This was indeed a handsome animal; when it turned its head from the shadows to the sunlight, the fur shone like metal. But from the gorgeous ornaments on the horse's legs, I knew that this horse must not be the neighbor's rented horse. "Whose horse is this?" I asked Julie, who had just moved the small footstool next to the last wooden stake near me. "This horse?" she said, standing on tiptoe on the footstool to hang the clothes, "It belongs to that foreign university student, I don't know what his name is." I looked up at her, but she didn't turn her head, she was still hanging her clothes. I was getting impatient when I suddenly heard a voice behind me saying, "Miss Nali, forget it, it's already hung up!"

"I also saw how she let her arms fall down and quickly lowered the rolled-up clothes; when I turned my head, I only saw that noble, pale-faced youth standing in front of me, Nali didn't say a word and jumped down from the footstool to stand beside me. That young gentleman also just stood there, his eyes only on Nali, as if he had forgotten everything. "I've met a ghost!" I thought, so I casually said something about the golden chestnut horse, I kept talking until someone answered me; but unconsciously all three of us walked across the yard. The horse stomped the ground with its hooves and looked at its master with smart eyes. Nali stood beside the horse, stroking the smooth horse neck with her hand, showing a very envious look. "This horse is as tame as a sheep," the young gentleman said, "Miss Nali, would you like to ride for a while? There is also a woman's saddle hanging in the stable?" She shook her head; but I heard her breathing shorten, she was indeed emitting a happy glow. This Count understood her thoughts very well, because he gave a wink, and others put the saddle on the horse's back and installed a light bridle. Nali looked at the saddle, her eyes as if bewitched. But when the groom put the wooden step for mounting in front of her, the young gentleman moved the stool aside. "No need for this, John!" he shouted, and he naturally picked up the little girl with one hand. "Put your feet firmly in the palm of my hand!" he said, extending his other hand in front of her, while raising his head to gaze at her. Nali seemed to obey his orders, putting her small feet in the Count's hand. I saw the Count hesitate for a moment, but only for a moment, then he sent her onto the horse with a quick motion.

"She sat on the saddle, her face flustered, her eyes cast down, and patiently let him entangle the reins between his fingers. The horse shook its head and let out a long hiss. Its master stroked the silky mane a few times, then placed one hand on the saddle behind Nali's back, while the other hand held the bridle and slowly pulled the horse to circle the cemetery."

"I must say, these two young people were a perfect match; anyone who saw her like this would never have thought that this beautiful girl was just a seamstress, a tailor's daughter!"

"Soon she complained that the horse was not going fast enough. She waved her hand, and the horse began to trot, and the young gentleman let go and retreated to the grass. But he did not leave her for a moment, as the horse ran, he also circled with the whip; he was like crazy, his eyes constantly fixed on the little girl, from her black hair fluttering in the wind, to the small feet peeking out from under her clothes on the saddle. He sometimes shouted at her, and sometimes said a few words to the horse. The horse ran faster and faster, panting, waving its tail in the air. Nali simply didn't pay attention to this. She just sat there distracted, smiling at the young gentleman, her eyes fixed on him, as if he was supporting her on the saddle."
