Supplement to the Shanghai News

Discussions

Saving Disaster Through Thrift 177

— Qiong Sheng

When the drought demon raged last year, our contemporary worthies said: After human disasters, comes natural disasters; it is roughly "good fortune never comes in pairs, but bad luck never comes alone," this year we have suffered both human disasters and natural disasters! From the coast of Guangdong in the south to the land of Shandong in the north, news reports came that the fragmented Chinese mainland was almost half submerged in water, and floods were rampant! Li, Fan, Yanshi, the entire cities were submerged, Yisha and other places were like swamps. More than one hundred disaster-stricken counties, millions of refugees, houses, fields, livestock, and people, were swept into the water and lost their lives, the exact number of which is unknown! If we are allowed to ignore the words "human affairs are not well managed," many "compassionate" people will surely scratch their heads and stomp their feet, beat their chests and weep, and shout, "Heaven does not pity us, sending down this great calamity!"

Compassion is certainly compassion, but this compassion still cannot break the shocking contrast between the wails of refugees, starving and waiting for death, on the one hand, and the cars, horses, clothing, and music, forgetting their worries, on the other. In the dance halls, one cannot hear the sounds of cannons from northern Shanghai, and in the air-conditioned rooms, how can one see the disaster victims crying for food? Truly, "if one were to treat people with benevolence, how could one go so far!"

However, "treat people as siblings, and regard all creatures as companions," as the ancients have taught. Moreover, we are all in the same boat, all descendants of the Yellow Emperor. Therefore, Mr. Ma Xiangbo, an old man of ninety-six, with this in mind, earnestly appealed, "May our countrymen look down and appreciate his sincerity": "Those who wear silk and wrap themselves in Shu brocade should think of the disaster victims who are naked and bare; those who drink fragrant liquor and eat rich food should think of the disaster victims who gnaw tree bark and chew grass roots; those who live in high halls and reside in mansions should think of the disaster victims who nest in treetops and live in earthen mounds; those who ride swift horses and drive jeweled carriages should think of the disaster victims who are submerged in floods and float on the surging waves," and "humbly presents the proposal of saving disaster through thrift to the countrymen." Of course, we also believe that dancing on eggs will inevitably lead to breakage. "If one were to treat people with benevolence," everyone would agree with this act of saving disaster through thrift. In particular, the phenomenon that Ma Xiangbo called "when the fields are full of starving people, I alone eat my fill; when everyone is sleeping in the open, I alone live in comfort," is truly unreasonable!

The reason why this unreasonable fact must be repeatedly mentioned to the people is not only to despise it, but also to be seriously vigilant! Because in recent years, there have been ladies who "dare not lag behind in patriotism," "saving the country through dancing," and "integrating patriotism with entertainment," which has been adopted by them as a great principle of "working together." We can predict that these gentlemen and ladies, while seeking pleasure, will raise this banner and fear that they will greatly express their compassion and carry out the "righteous deeds" of disaster relief!

Mr. Ma Xiangbo's movement to save disaster through thrift, I think, should not be a talisman for gentlemen and ladies to seek pleasure, and it should not help them make that kind of pleasure and "righteous deeds" "truly deserved," that is its meaning.

Home 178

— Right and Wrong

Since leaving my hometown and living a vagrant life, though on the surface I deceive myself by saying how free and unfettered this life is, whenever I am sick or encounter adversity, I always yearn for the loveliness and warmth of home!

If I had a home, when I was sick, I wouldn't be abandoned in a corner alone, groaning and suffering. Even if I wanted to vent my grievances, who would listen to such disheartening words? Everyone else has a home that I don't! If I had a home, when I hit a wall, I wouldn't be weeping silently in a corner alone. You want to tell people about your grievances? People don't like to hear such unpleasant things; everyone else has a home that I don't!

But can I guarantee that I won't get sick, can I always float and sink in the sea of humanity as I wish? Eventually, there will be a time when my hair is full of white. At that time, home is even more lovely and precious. "Old age without a home" is the most tear-jerking phrase in my hometown!

I am already a middle-aged man nearing the end of my life. In this way, I spend half of my long days living a wandering life. Although in a corner of the world, I have a warm home, and I am the only son of a pampered child. Because of my departure, my father published the most moving words in the newspaper asking me to return. Every day I read the words of repentance called out from the depths of my father's heart. He has already felt the painful plea of "old age without a home." A warm home was deprived of its happiness because of that wanton stepmother. He couldn't even protect the only son of his previous wife, causing me to suffer such a fate in my youth. I deeply feel my father's pain, and I want to forget that humiliation and throw myself into his arms. But in reality, it will only make things worse. When I reappear in the home, perhaps my father's pain will be even greater. Let me sacrifice my own happiness so that my father can have a home in his old age!

But I am already middle-aged, and nearing the twilight of my life. Seeing the harmonious families of my friends, I am so envious that it stirs up a feeling of helpless annoyance. So, my friends either openly or secretly urge me to get married, but I always smile and don't answer.

I remember someone saying that a wife and a toilet are the main conditions for a home. To have a home, I naturally have to get married. But is marriage such an easy thing? A lonely stranger in a foreign land cannot have such extravagant hopes. When I was young, I had a love affair, but now I am left with only bitter memories.

According to news from my hometown, my father always thinks about his son who left home. I wish him longevity. One day, I will bring a pure heart and throw myself into my father's arms to repent. I belong to that "home"!

The Mind of an Old Man 179

— Qi Yun

On a quiet summer night, the silent streets are bathed in water-like clear moonlight, and the dark blue sky, slightly bright, is inlaid with smiling stars. Wandering alone in the serene quiet of the night, my heart feels old.

Turning a corner, unexpectedly, lowering my head, I see my own stumbling, thin shadow. The closer it gets to the street lamp, the fainter it becomes, as if it is being swallowed by the listless light. My old heart is even more filled with a desolate mood.

The clear outline shown in the moonlight, but the thin shadow reflected by the listless street lamp, truly symbolizes my own melancholy and gloomy life!

Since I first stepped into the circle of life, it has been as if a lark has been locked in a cage. Never again will the so-called beautiful, happy days of spring arrive. Not only the fervent desires, hopes, and yearnings originally hidden in the hearts of young people, like reefs or embankments resisting the turbulent seawater, all turn into foam, quietly receding and disappearing; moreover, from then on, I am cut off from the kingdom of purity, innocence, and naivete, and helplessly, unwillingly, I step into another hell full of deceit, hypocrisy, and treachery. — All day long, I am buried in the bad atmosphere of merchants and businessmen, gritting my teeth and enduring the insidious, vicious, and oppressive behavior between people, and the laughter with hidden daggers.

But, I should learn the ways of life! — Because, the road of life, especially this journey from leaving the kingdom of childhood and entering society, is a rugged Sichuan path. — Cold eyes, discrimination, squeezing, being betrayed by others... these are the trials that are meant to be, how painful it is to be a person!

Therefore, I have now learned to be indifferent and silent.

My mind, which always loved romantic novels and movies, has also begun to change. Now, I only like to immerse myself in the bitterness of the world and experience more of the so-called "ways of the world."

Life, the demon that torments the passion of young people!

But, who can avoid life (the ugly factors of reality) and survive?

Ah, what a pitiful and admirable thing!

Torrent 180

— Ye Fei

Clang clang clang! Clang clang clang! Clang… clang… clang…

——Everyone, hurry to the rescue! The east embankment of the southern village has been washed away by the flood!

The families in the village were awakened from their sleep. Everyone, hearing such a terrifying cry, Jin Gen and Uncle San De jumped out of bed without even putting on their clothes. They went to the door and saw groups of people flowing outside. The sound of gongs and the cries were constantly echoing in the village. The shouts of women and the cries of children shook the entire world.

The rain poured down as if it were being dumped, and a sense of complete submersion filled everyone's heart!

"Alas! The heavens are really killing and setting fires. If the east embankment collapses, will any of us in the entire village survive?" Old Lady A Qi mumbled, touching the wall as she walked.

"Flood, flood! I never thought there would be a flood here," Sister-in-law Ren Sheng rolled out of bed and opened the door to take a look. She saw countless torches flickering under the eaves, and many long shadows moving messily across the muddy ground, all rushing and shouting in a frantic manner.

Clang clang clang! Clang clang clang! Clang… clang… clang… clang…

——The more people, the better, hurry up! Please bring iron rakes, ropes, and poles!

The sound of feet treading through puddles mixed with the shouts, forming a chaotic scene. Groups of people surged towards the southern village.

"Uncle San De, hurry!"

"Jin Gen, why aren't you hurrying? The water is about to rush into the village!"

Everyone blamed each other, but there was nothing they could do except worry about each other.

The low-lying areas around the east embankment had completely turned into a swamp, and the water was still rising steadily. A stone tablet on the bank was submerged, and then water entered the Yuwang Temple. The embankment had long been washed away.

Although people were crowded together like ants, a few torches flickered under the corridor of the Yuwang Temple, illuminating the pale faces of everyone, adding a layer of tragic color. Everyone was soaked through like drowned chickens.

"Block it, block it quickly! If we let it rush in again, we won't be able to hold on!" Drunkard Jin You shouted desperately from the high bank on the right!

"Don't shout! First, saw pine trees to drive stakes, otherwise the mud and stones will be washed away."

"Stones, stones, quickly carry stones over here."

"Carry mud, quickly! Quickly! There's no time!"

Yellow mud and stones were thrown haphazardly towards the breach, but the force of the rushing water was very strong, so despite being piled up, it would all be washed away. Heads moved like waves under the heavy rain. Although it was already getting light, the rain still didn't stop, and the raging waves in the breach kept flowing inward, from one foot to one and a half feet, and then two feet...

The people doing the rescue were initially just able-bodied young men, but later even the elderly and many women, and even the larger children, went to help. They worked all night carrying mud and moving stones, and they were as exhausted as old silkworms. However, the滔滔 flood kept inundating the land. Before noon on the second day, the entire village had become an ocean. The furniture and belongings of many families were floating on the water. People climbed on trees or roofs to seek help, some crying, some shouting. Life was only on the line of death. There were also many floating corpses on the water.

Miao Women 181

— Especially

Starting from Sichuan, walking along the mountain roads of Sichuan and Guizhou, passing through the county town of Qijiang, and reaching the border of Guizhou. If you pay attention, soon you will know that the Universe people reside here, and maybe you can see a posture of Miao people's lives.

Indeed, Miao people are rarely seen in civilized cities, or it can simply be said that they do not exist. In order to live, they may be unwilling to go to other provinces to operate things, so here, in the mountain depressions, they have planted very deep roots.

Needless to say, the mountain depressions are very inconvenient for travelers. Without the tools of transportation, the outside air is blocked. Naturally, due to the trend of nature, a very obvious regression is presented, but the prosperity between capitals is constantly progressing. Because of this, no matter how difficult your mountain depression is, its civilization can still penetrate a little.

Perhaps it was a coincidence of opportunity? On the second day of entering Huangzhou, I discovered the activities of Miao women jumping and leaping before our eyes.

What kind of people are they? At first, I asked, with a surprised expression.

Miao people, said Zhang Futou. There are many here.

I didn't say anything more, but in terms of dress and language, it did give me a novel feeling, but this feeling soon subsided.

Some people say that small ethnic groups can be assimilated by large ethnic groups. For the sake of practical needs, there must be no interruption of exchanges between each other. In this way, gradually, from language habits to daily life, everything is changing from a distant distance to a close harmony. Although there are still some differences in clothing, there are also some who hide in the deep valleys where few people are seen, practicing self-enjoying cultivation and food.

Perhaps it is their unique character. In transactions, they are mostly handled by women. What they handle is mostly mobile peddling, from here to there, or calculating when there will be a "market."

Why not open a shop for more comfortable transactions? This is not that they don't want to, but they are bound by economic forces, and, dealing with sophisticated tactics with sincere experience, the result is a strong component of failure.

No matter where, in order to resist the invasion of depression, they are similarly being eroded. Here, panic whips their hearts. Some also abandon their families and are hired by others, and some go to collect natural products in the mountains that do not cost capital to carry to the market to peddle. If you are in the provincial capital, you can hear the cries of Miao women selling.

When summer is about to end, the mountain products are ripe and yellow. Then, listen:

—Buy it, big wild pears! (Note)

However, when summer has slipped past, and when the wild pear season has passed, you will never feel silence. Other words will crisply leap into your ears.

The clothes are all made of homespun cloth. Love of beauty is human nature. Some people add colors to the homespun cloth by printing, or weave patterns from cotton thread. The sleeves are so wide, like a monk's. The lower body wears a pleated skirt, the legs and feet are bare, and long cloth strips like soldiers' leggings are tied from below the knee to the ankle. The feet wear straw sandals, and the head is wrapped in a cloth ring. Some also insert a few silver hairpins into their hair. In this way, it is very sufficient to boast among them.

If possible, buying a little of their woven "Miao brocade" is very detailed.

In short, their physique is strong, their spirit is enduring, and they have the instinct to be self-reliant. Women who are influenced by the material civilization between cities cannot be compared.

Note: Wild pear, a kind of plant in the mountains, round and thorny, containing a sour taste.

Amateur Mailbox

Can a Widow Request Property Division? 182

Editor:

I have a younger sister who is twenty-one years old. She married a certain gentleman two years ago. Unexpectedly, a few months ago, the gentleman passed away due to illness. Her parents-in-law see that she is very young and has not had any children, so they strongly advocate that she remarry. Because of her love relationship with her deceased husband, she is reluctant to talk about the issue of remarriage for a while, so others do not actively persuade her to remarry. However, her deceased husband has several brothers, who have all married sisters-in-law. They see that my younger sister is young and often bully her, so there is a general inability to live together between the sisters-in-law. Now that her parents-in-law have not died, my younger sister still has support. If the two old people pass away, wouldn't her uncles and aunts-in-law bully her even more? At that time, she will be isolated and helpless, and my family is not wealthy, so her life will definitely be in danger. Therefore, she wants to request a property division before her parents-in-law die in order to seek future security. I don't know if a widow has the right to request property division from her in-laws? Can her uncles and aunts-in-law prevent it? Please give me an answer.

Respectfully,

Ge Changsheng

Editor's Note: Ge Jun's in-laws are able to break the old habits of ordinary people and think about the future happiness of their daughter-in-law after their son's death, and advise her to remarry. Their thinking is really admirable. As for his sister being reluctant to talk about remarriage for a while, that is also human nature. In the near future, there is no need to actively persuade her, so as not to cause her painful memories. We can only wait and see for opportunities to talk about it again.

The current laws stipulate that children may not request an analysis of their parents' property, but exceptions may be allowed in special circumstances. For example, "The relationship between a widow and her in-laws, or between a legitimate child and a stepmother, has become like strangers, and it is difficult to force them together, so they are allowed to separate their property and live separately." Now, Ge Jun's sister and her in-laws are certainly not in the "like strangers, it is difficult to force them together" degree; but if there is concrete evidence between uncles and aunts-in-law sufficient to prove that there is an urgent need for future life security, a request for property division can also be made.

According to the letter, her in-laws do not seem to have bad feelings towards her, so it is best to directly explain the difficulties to her in-laws and ask them to make the decision. I think they may have better ways to help her.

Shenbao Architecture Weekly

The Method of Cofferdam for Bridge Pier Construction 188

— Xiao Ang

The Qiantang River Bridge has been under construction for several months. The magnitude of the project is truly rare in the country. Xiao Ang took the opportunity of his internship in Hangzhou to meet with Engineer Zhang of the engineering office. That evening, a certain American bridge expert gave a public academic lecture, elaborating on the construction of caissons in great detail. After listening, Xiao Ang had the opportunity to see the construction site firsthand, gaining much knowledge. This is now described in detail below for public research.

The solidity of the bridge piers is crucial to the life of the entire bridge. While damage to the bridge body is relatively easy to repair, the collapse of the bridge piers means the end of the entire bridge. The method of pier construction varies depending on the location, taking into account the flow rate of the river, the structure of the riverbed, the depth of the water, and the judgment of the architects. Generally, it can be divided into three types:

(1) Cofferdam method - used for river depths of 15 feet or less;

(2) Pneumatic caisson method - used for depths of less than 110 feet;

(3) Deep excavation method - used when the river water is extremely deep. The cofferdam method is described below. The other two methods will be detailed in a separate article later.

The cofferdam method involves surrounding the pier construction site with an impermeable and solid dam on all four sides, and then pumping the water out of the dam using a water pump. The bridge piers are then built inside this dry dam. This method is inexpensive and easy to work with, but it is difficult to control the pressure and seepage of the river water, so it is generally not used in river depths of more than 15 feet. If steel sheet piles are driven on all four sides, the depth can be increased to 35 feet, but for safety reasons, this is rarely used. Moreover, if the river water level fluctuates unpredictably, this method becomes quite difficult. Depending on the materials used, cofferdams can be divided into the following:

(1) Earth cofferdam - This dam is made of soil. Because soil is not very strong and is very permeable, a large amount of soil is used and it occupies a large area. It is generally not used if there is no large source of soil nearby or if the river water is slightly deep and fast-flowing.

(2) Stone cofferdam - This dam is made of stacked rocks and coated with mud to prevent leakage through the gaps. This method is less expensive, as both work and materials are more economical.

(3) Sandbag cofferdam - This method uses sandbags stacked to form a cofferdam. The thickness depends on the depth of the water. Because sandbags are movable, it is considered convenient.

(4) Wooden cofferdam - The dam is made of wooden planks interlocked and driven into the riverbed. To prevent leakage between the seams, some use two layers, while others cover the seams with wooden strips. This method is only used if the riverbed is layered with soft material.

(5) Reinforced concrete cofferdam - This dam is constructed on the bank in two layers, inner and outer. It can be floated to the work site and sunk to the riverbed using heavy objects. The riverbed is covered with mud to seal the bottom to prevent seepage.

(6) Ice cofferdam - This method surrounds the river water with non-conductive materials in the shape of a cofferdam, and then uses a method to freeze the enclosed water. This method is the least expensive, but it is not easy to do well.

Building piers using the cofferdam method has many difficulties, such as when the sand layer of the riverbed is too thick, the dam foundation is not solid, spring water comes from the riverbed, preventing the water inside the dam from being completely pumped out, as well as unexpected tides and the collapse of the dam wall. These are all problems that the builders must solve at any time and in any place.

Tales of Architectural History (1) 189

— Buren

Before history began, there was no architecture in terms of mankind. The earliest houses were extremely crude and simple, made by gathering the most readily available materials in the easiest way. Huts made of branches, walls made of stones, cabins made of wood—such houses had no other meaning than to provide shelter from the wind and rain. Humans lived in such dwellings, which were almost indistinguishable from nests, for hundreds of thousands of years. Then, the Egyptians, whose civilization was developed, began to build houses that belonged to proper architectural forms. These houses were works that belonged only to humans and not to any other animals.

The Egyptians had many fine and easily workable stones suitable for building, and the climate was excellent, without frost, dew, or fog. Therefore, those buildings that have not been destroyed by human power still exist and are almost as perfect as when they were first built. The solidity and grandeur of these buildings make it impossible for later generations to destroy them. This was the original intention of the ancient Egyptian kings in building them in that way. What they most desired was to create immortal tombs in which to store their mummies. However, although the ancient Egyptian kings planned their tombs after death to be more elaborate than their residences when they were alive, there are still many relics of magnificent palaces and slightly grotesque and mysterious temples.

We believe that the tyrannical ancient Egyptian kings could never have created their massive monuments without a people full of obedience and tens of thousands of slaves and prisoners of war, because the tools and machines of the time were very simple, and there was no way to haul and place those huge and cumbersome stones except by relying on the strength of humans and animals. Indeed, without having to rely on the inscriptions on the buildings, we can infer very accurately from the buildings themselves what kind of society Egypt was at the time. The huge pillars of palaces and tombs still stand, serving as evidence of the lifestyle of the Egyptians at that time.

In Syria and Persia, grand temples were also being built. "Chaldean priests" observed celestial phenomena from the upper levels of these temples and predicted the future. Egyptian architecture used stone beams, while Syrian and Persian architecture added brick-built arcades and domes. Greek architecture, although not using arcades and domes, was evolved from these early experiments.

The earliest Greek architecture we know of was crude and robust, such as wooden temples that imitated stone temples. The early wooden temples decorated with bronze have long since collapsed. However, gradually, the Greeks became the most prominent architects, and their architects and sculptors were at least equal to any predecessors or successors.

The Acropolis of Athens (a lovely, tall temple citadel), mostly built in the 15th century BC, has always been and still is one of the wonders of the world. These multi-columned buildings made of honey-colored marble can be said to be perfect buildings. Their proportions, their patterns of light and shadow, the size and position of their columns, their inlays, their clean carvings—everything seems correct and appropriate.

From Architectural Art to Greek Temples (3) 190

— Sun Zongwen

——The Most Glorious Page in the History of World Architecture——

(II) Characteristics of Greek Temple Architecture

When discussing the characteristics of Greek temple architecture, we can divide them into several points. For the sake of brevity, it is roughly divided into (A) Orientation, (B) Roof, (C) Doors and Windows, (D) Capitals, (F) Stepped Stones, (E) Building Materials, etc. These are now described separately below:

(A) Orientation The most important factor in the construction of Greek temples is the "orientation issue." Because we know that the purpose of a temple is to be inhabited by a "god"; and the Greeks believed that gods had the closest relationship with natural objects, especially the sun, which was the most mysterious: therefore, the orientation of the temple had a close relationship with the sun. As everyone knows, the morning sun rises from the east and sets in the west. Therefore, when the Greeks built temples, the direction of the main entrance was often facing east. The entrance faces directly towards the shrine, the only reason being that the temple was to be inhabited by a god, and the sun in the world rises from the east. Therefore, when the Greek people went to the temple every morning to worship the gods, the light shone directly into the surroundings of the god because the eastward-facing entrance faced directly the shrine; the meaning of this being that people could see everything about the god very clearly and brightly. This refers to the Greek aspect. As for the temples in Egypt, their orientation was not based on the daytime sun, but on the constellations in the night sky as the standard. Although this does not fall within the scope of this article, for reference purposes, I will now briefly list several examples of various buildings whose orientation is based on the orientation of constellations, in order to see a glimpse of the relationship between "temples and orientation."

1. Between 5300 BC and 1850 BC, the temples of Egypt were built according to the light of Sirius rising, which could shine into the god's eyes in the sanctuary.

2. Temples in Eottu and other places in Egypt were mostly built according to the light of Canopus before sunrise, which could shine into the god's eyes in the sanctuary. Temples in Caruac and other places were built according to the light of Canopus at sunset, which could shine into the god's eyes.

3. The oldest temple of Dendera, around 7000 BC, was built facing the constellation Vega.

4. The Egyptians and Greeks often called Arcturus the "star of the temple," indicating an important target for seasonal changes.

From the four examples above, we can prove that the orientation of temple buildings has a very close relationship with the sun and constellations, so-called mysterious objects of nature!

(B) Roof There are many forms of Greek temple architecture. According to a famous Roman architect, there are about 13 types of plans for Greek temples. However, in general, the structure of the temple hall is roughly rectangular, surrounded by various capitals, with no windows on the left, right, or rear sides, and the front and rear parts are narrower than the two sides. The roofs of all temples are uniformly triangular, called a Pediment. On it, various commemorative patterns are carved with extremely exquisite techniques to embellish and decorate it. The external form of the roof is generally triangular, which is sufficient to express its true spirit, showing that its internal engineering structure is the same, and there is absolutely no trace of false decoration on it. From this, we can see a glimpse of the Greek people's national character of being non-hypocritical and not making falsehoods, and faithfully expressing themselves. This is revealed in the roof.

(C) Doors and Windows The unique feature of Greek temples in terms of architecture also lies in the issue of doors and windows; because the temple is never opened with windows on all sides (although later, the Temple of Apollo appeared, because the position of the shrine inside was not built in the center, but built on the side, and because the construction direction of the main entrance was facing north, so on the east side of the wall, a window was opened on the wall of the temple for the first time; in this way, the morning sunlight could shine directly onto the statue from the window. In this way, although there are temples with windows opened on the walls, they are ultimately a minority among the minority; it can also be said that they are exceptions.) It only opened a door on the eastward-facing wall for people to worship the gods; but, speaking of which, the issue of light in the hall becomes somewhat doubtful. Because the light shining in from the small entrance is definitely not enough for a large hall to control and use. Wouldn't the hall feel dark? However, we also believe that because the internal building materials mostly use luminescent substances such as marble, gold, silver, and gems; and the inside of the roof is probably paved entirely with marble slabs. Therefore, from this point, we can infer the possibility that there are no windows on all sides. There are also some people who advocate that there are windows opened on the roof; but we have no way to verify this from the excavated relics. Because the remains of the roof are rarely left to the present day, this question cannot be adequately proven, even until now.
